And the author of this book, upon completing for you, my children, this book which is a part of medical knowledge in its entirety and achieving clarity and explanation within it, saw fit to complete it for you with this chapter which is a part of practical work by hand.
For practical work by hand is improved in our country and in our time utterly absent, so much so that its science is nearly studied and its influence discontinued. And what remains of it are slight illustrations in the books of the early scholars, which have been distorted by hands and subjected to errors and confusion, until its meanings have become obscure and its benefits distant.
So I saw fit to revive it and compose this chapter in the manner of explanation and clarification, providing images of cautery blades and other surgical instruments, as this adds to the clarity and is essential for what is needed.
The reason there is no skilled craftsman in our time is because the practice of medicine is long and its practitioner should first train in the science of anatomy, which Galen described. Until one becomes knowledgeable about the benefits of the organs, their forms, their temperaments, their connections and disconnections, the knowledge of bones, nerves, muscles, their numbers, their origins, and the locations of the arteries and veins and their origins.
For this reason, Hippocrates said that there are many who are called doctors but few in practice, especially in the art of the hand. We have mentioned some of this in the introduction of this book.
For whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have mentioned regarding anatomy is likely to make a mistake that could kill people, as I have witnessed many who have presumed knowledge in this field and claimed it without actual knowledge or understanding.
That is because I saw an ignorant doctor who cut into a goiter on the neck of a woman, thus cutting some arteries in the neck, causing the woman's blood to flow until she fell dead before him.
I saw another doctor who proceeded to remove a stone from an elderly man, and the stone was large, so he took a risk and removed it along with a piece of the bladder. The man died around three days later, and I had been called to remove it, but when I saw the condition of the stone and the patient, I determined that it was beyond what could be managed.
I saw another doctor who was employed by some of the officials in our city to practice medicine.
A young black boy had a fracture in his leg near the ankle along with a wound, and the doctor, out of ignorance, quickly bound the fracture tightly over the wound with bandages and splints without leaving any room for the wound to breathe.
Then he let him go to his desires, and left him for days, ordering him not to loosen the binding until his leg and foot swelled up and he was on the verge of death.
I was called to him, so I quickly loosened the binding, and he found relief and was alleviated from his pains, except that the corruption had already taken hold in the limb and I could not prevent it.
The corruption continued to spread in the limb until he perished.
I saw another doctor who cut into a cancerous tumor, and it ulcerated after days until the sufferer's condition greatly worsened. This is because if the cancer is purely of a black bile mixture, then it should never be treated with surgery at all.
unless it is in a limb that could possibly be amputated entirely.
And for this, my son, you should know that working with the hand is divided into two parts: work accompanied by safety and work that often results in damage.
And I have warned in every place in this book about work that involves risk and fear; you should beware of it and reject it.
So that the ignorant may not find a way to criticize or attack, take for yourselves firmness and caution, and for your patients, gentleness and thoroughness.
Use the best methods leading to safety and a praised outcome, and avoid dangerous and difficult-to-cure diseases.
Purify yourselves from what you fear may bring doubt into your religion and worldly affairs, for it is more lasting for your honor and raises your status in this world and the hereafter.
For Galen said in one of his admonitions: Do not treat bad diseases and thus be called bad doctors.
And I have divided this article into three chapters.
The first chapter.
On cauterization with fire and cauterization with sharp medicines, organized and arranged from head to foot, including images of the instruments and cauterizing blades, and everything needed for working by hand.
And the second chapter.
On incision, cauterization, bloodletting, cupping, surgeries, and the extraction of arrows and similar procedures, all are organized in chapters and arranged with illustrations of the instruments.
And the third chapter.
On bone setting, dislocations, and the treatment of gout and similar conditions, organized and arranged from head to foot with illustrations of the instruments.
The first chapter.
On cauterization.
And before we mention working with it, it is necessary to mention the manner of its benefits and harms and in what temperament it is used.
I say that the discussion on the manner of the benefit of cauterization and its harms is a long discourse, a precise science, and a hidden secret, and many wise people have spoken about it.
They differed on this, and I have summarized the little from their discourse to avoid lengthiness.
I say that cauterization generally benefits every bad temperament whether with matter or without, except for two temperaments: the hot temperament without matter and the dry temperament without matter.
As for the dry temperament with matter, they differed on it. Some said that cauterization is beneficial in it, while others said the opposite, that cauterization is not suitable for a disease caused by heat and dryness because the nature of fire is heat and dryness.
It is impossible to cure a hot and dry disease with a hot and dry treatment. Those who argue the opposite say that cauterization with fire can be beneficial for a hot and dry disease that occurs in people's bodies. For when you add the body of the human and its moisture to the temperament of fire, you affect the body of the human with cold.
And I say with his saying because experience has revealed that to me many times, but this matter should not be imagined except by one who has trained and practiced in the art of cauterization to a great extent. And he recognized the differences in people's temperaments and the state of diseases in themselves, their causes, their symptoms, and the duration of time they last.
And as for the other temperaments, there is no need for you to fear them, especially the cold and moist diseases, for all physicians agree on them and do not disagree about the benefit of cauterization in them.
Know, my sons, that one of the secrets of treatment is cauterization with fire and its advantage over cauterization with a burning medicine because fire is a single essence and its effect does not extend beyond the organ which was cauterized and it does not harm another connected organ except with a slight damage.
And cauterization with burning medicine may extend its effect to other organs and may cause a disease in the organ that is difficult to treat, and may even cause death. But fire, due to its nobility and the generosity of its essence, does not do this unless it is excessive.
And this has become clear to us through experience due to the length of service, attention to the craft, and understanding the realities of the matter.
And for this reason, I have dispensed with lengthy discourse, but were it not inappropriate for my book, I would present to you a mysterious secret about fire and its manner of action on bodies and its removal of diseases with philosophical and demonstrative speech that penetrates your understanding.
And know, O sons, that they have differed about the time in which cauterization is appropriate, and they made the best time the spring season.
And I say that cauterization may be appropriate at all times, because the harm caused by the time is overshadowed by the benefit brought about by cauterization. Especially if the cauterization is for severe, necessary pains that are dangerous and cannot tolerate delay, due to the fear that it may result in a disaster that is greater than the slight harm caused by the time.
Do not let it come to your mind, O sons, what the common people and ignorant physicians imagine, that cauterization which cures a disease will never return, and they consider it permanent.
It is not as they imagine, for cauterization is like a medicine that alters the temperament and dries the humidities which are the cause of pains.
However, cauterization is preferred over medicine due to its quick success, strong effect, and intense power.
And the disease may return at some time, depending on the condition of the patient, the strength and dominance of his illness, and what accumulates in his body from excesses and neglecting himself in acquiring them from foods and other such causes.
Except that the disease in which cauterization is used is a mild one and in an organ with little excess and moisture. Like extracting the tooth from pain and the like, it may be that such pain does not return, and this happens in the least.
And as for the common people's saying that cauterization is the last of medicine, it is a correct statement not in accordance with what they believe, because they think that no treatment, whether with medication or otherwise, can be beneficial after cauterization, but the matter is contrary to that.
The meaning of "cauterization is the last of medicine" is that when we use various treatments for a disease and those medicines are ineffective, then we use cauterization as the final method, which may be effective. Hence comes the saying that "cauterization is the last of medicine. Not in the sense that the common people and many ignorant physicians have understood it.
The early scholars mentioned that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron. They said this because gold is balanced and its essence is noble, and they claimed that the site of cauterization does not suppurate. However, this is not always the case.
For I have tried this and found that it only occurs in some bodies and not others. Cauterization with gold is indeed better and more preferable than with iron, as they claimed. However, when you heat the cautery instrument made of gold in fire, it is not clear to you when it has reached the desired level of heat due to the redness of the gold.
Because it quickly cools down, and if you increase the heat, it melts in the fire and becomes molten, causing the craftsman to be troubled by this. Therefore, cauterization with iron is faster and closer to being correct for practical use, if God wills.
I have arranged this chapter on cauterization in sections organized from head to foot to make it easier for the student to find what he desires, God willing.
The first chapter.
Cauterization of the head is done once.
This cauterization is beneficial for excess moisture and cold that overpower the brain, which are causes of headache, frequent discharges from the head to the region of the eyes and ears, excessive sleep, tooth pain, and throat pains. In general, for every disease that occurs due to cold, such as paralysis, epilepsy, strokes, and other similar diseases.
The procedure for this cauterization is to first order the patient to purge with a laxative that cleanses the head for three or four nights, according to what is required by the strength of the patient, his age, and his habits.
Then order him to shave his head with a razor, then seat him in front of you, sitting cross-legged with his hands on his chest.
Then place the base of your palm on the base of his nose between his eyes, and where your middle finger ends, mark that spot with ink.
Then heat the olive-shaped cautery, which looks like this.
If the bone becomes exposed, about the size of a clove or a grain of carob, lift your hand. Otherwise, reapply with the same iron or another if it has cooled. Until you see what I have mentioned to you from the bone, then take some salt and dissolve it in water and soak a cotton piece in it and place it on the area and leave it for three days.
Then apply cotton soaked in fat to it and leave it until the inflammation subsides, then treat it with the four-part ointment until it heals, if God wills.
They have said that the wound is better and more beneficial the longer it remains open to discharge pus.
Some have mentioned that the skin should be cauterized down to the bone, and the cautery iron should be held until part of the thickness of the bone is burned. Then, what has been burnt from the bone should be removed and treated afterwards.
Others have said that cauterization should be intensified until it strongly affects the bone, causing pieces to fall off like carats or small disks. They claimed that this releases vapors from the head and leaves the wound open for a long time.
Then it should be treated until it heals. I do not approve of these types of cauterization except in some cases and as a risky method, and leaving them is better in my opinion. If it is safe, then the head weakens when its natural connection is disrupted, as we have observed with other organs.
This is especially true when the patient's head is naturally weak. The first type of cauterization is safer and better in my opinion, and it is what I use. Follow it and you will be safe, if God wills.
Chapter Two.
For the head as well.
If a chronic pain occurs in the head region and persists for a long time with the patient having used various treatments such as bloodletting, purgatives, fumigation, ointments, and dressings, especially if single cauterization which we described has been applied and none of these treatments have been beneficial, then examine. If the patient's head is inherently strong in structure and not weak, and if he feels a severe coldness, apply another cauterization slightly above the previous one. Then cauterize each temple of his head until the thickness of the skin is reduced and the amount of bone exposed is as we described. Cauterize another spot at the back of his head in the area known as the axe, but be gentle with your hand in this case and do not expose the bone, for the patient will feel intense pain here unlike the pain of other cauterizations on the head. I will mention this cauterization in its proper place.
The cautery used for the temples and the back of the head should be milder than the one used for the center of the head. This is its description.
Chapter Three.
On cauterizing non-chronic migraine.
If pain accompanied by headache occurs on one side of the head and extends to the eye, make the patient vomit with medicines that cleanse the head and use all other treatments mentioned in the sections on diseases. If this is not effective, then cauterization should be applied in two ways. Either cauterization with the sharp, burning medicine or with iron.
As for cauterization with the burning medicine, it is to take one clove of garlic, peel it, and cut its ends from both sides, then incise the site of pain on the cheek with a broad lancet until there is a space under the skin large enough to hold the clove.
It is inserted under the skin until it disappears, then tightly bandage it with care. Leave it for about fifteen hours, then remove the bandage and take out the garlic. Leave the wound alone for two or three days, then proceed with treatment.
Place cotton soaked in grease until the area suppurates, then treat it with ointment until it heals, if God wills. If you prefer, you can do this with some of the burning medicines that I provided in the eighteenth article on burning medicines.
As for cauterizing with iron, it is done in this manner: heat the cautery iron which has this shape:.
It is called the nail-shaped cautery because its head resembles a nail, with some perforations and a small protrusion in the middle.
Then place it on the site of pain and hold your hand as you rotate the iron slightly, and the amount you burn from the thickness of the skin should be about half of it. Lift your hand so as not to burn the artery below, which could cause bleeding. Then soak some cotton in salt water and place it on the area and leave it for three days. Then apply the cotton with fat, then treat it with the ointment until it heals, if God wills.
And if you want, cauterize this sinus with the sharp end of the cautery iron, and be careful not to cut the artery in this non-chronic sinus especially.
Chapter Four.
On cauterizing the chronic sinus.
If you treat the sinus with the treatments we have mentioned and those described in the divisions of diseases, and the treatment is ineffective, and you see in the condition what cannot be managed by the initial cauterization with medication or fire as we have mentioned. You should heat the cauterizing knife until it turns white, then apply it to the site of pain in a line about half a finger long or so, and leave your hand once as you press it until it cuts through the artery and reaches near the bone.
However, you should be careful not to affect the jaw that moves during chewing, as burning its muscle or nerve can cause spasms.
Be cautious and watchful of the bleeding from the artery you have cut, for there is great danger in cutting it. Especially for those who do not know what they are doing and have not tried the method, it is better to refrain from performing the procedure.
The management of incidental bleeding from the artery will be discussed in detail in its place in the book, if God wills. If you see in the condition what cannot be managed by this cauterization.
I have seen the body of the sick person able to bear cauterization in the middle of the head as described, and treat the wound until it heals, God willing.
And if you wish, use the cauterization we mentioned in the chapter on artery forceps with the two-bladed iron, for it is better and more effective than this.
Chapter Five.
On cauterizing the pains of the ears.
If pain occurs in the ear due to cold and is treated with laxatives and other treatments we mentioned in the classification, but the pain does not subside, heat the iron known as the point, which has this shape.
Then apply it around the entire ear after heating it, as if circling around it, or around both ears if the pain is in both. Keep the cauterization slightly away from the base of the ear after marking the spot with ink. The cauterization should be about ten points in each ear or so. Then treat the areas until they heal, God willing.
Chapter Six.
On cauterizing the larynx.
The larynx that is treated with cauterization is of the type caused by phlegm, as I mentioned in the classifications of diseases.
Cauterization should be avoided for the type that occurs due to dryness and nerve spasms.
If you have treated this type of larynx with electuary, pessaries, and gargles but your treatment has not been effective, it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauteries. One is at the base of the ear, the second slightly below his temple, and the third at the meeting of the lips.
Make your cautery on the opposite side of the affected area because the relaxation occurs in the side that appears healthy.
The image of the cautery is to cauterize it slightly below the temple, opposite the upper part of the ear, and another in the temple area, with its length equal to the length of the thumb.
Lower your cautery until it burns to about half the thickness of the skin. This is the image of the iron, which is a type of knife that has been shown previously, but it is slightly finer as you can see. It is desirable that the knife should be slightly thicker, then treat the area as previously mentioned until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Seven.
On the cautery of chronic stroke.
If the stroke becomes chronic and the treatments we mentioned do not work and there is no fever in the patient, cauterize it with four cauteries. Place one cautery on each temple of his head, one in the center of the head as mentioned, and a cautery at the back of the head as previously described.
The description of the cautery is as previously mentioned, and it may also be cauterized at the mouth of the stomach for better effect, then treat it as previously described.
Chapter Eight.
In order to forget.
That which is due to phlegm should first be treated by giving the patient large draughts and purified seeds for the brain.
Then, his entire head should be shaved and a mustard poultice, as written in the chapter on poultices, should be applied to the back of his head multiple times, for this is a form of cauterization.
Do that in the same manner I described there, for he will be healed by it. If not, cauterize him three times at the back of his head, arranged from the top of the head to below the neck.
Make the space between each cauterization the thickness of a finger. Then, treat the cauterization as previously described. If you wish to increase the treatment and the patient can tolerate it, cauterize the middle area again.
If you wish to increase the treatment, cauterize him on the temples, then treat him until he is healed. The cautery should be olive-shaped as previously described.
Chapter Nine.
On the cauterization of paralysis and the relaxation of the entire body.
It is necessary to proceed with purifying the head with draughts and what we have mentioned. Then, shave the patient's head and cauterize it with one cautery in the center of the head, one on each temple, and one at the back.
And three on the vertebrae of the neck, and if you need for the condition of bodily weakness more than that, and the patient can tolerate it and the disease is strong and established, cauterize four burnings on the vertebrae of his back. And continue with the cauterization until it burns most of the skin, then lift your hand, and then treat it as previously mentioned until it heals, if God wills, and the cautery iron should be olive-shaped.
The Tenth Chapter.
On the cauterization of epilepsy.
Only the epileptic who has epilepsy due to phlegm should be cauterized; his brain should first be cleansed with large electuaries and all other treatments which we mentioned in the division, if the patient is an adult and can tolerate taking medications.
If it is a child who cannot tolerate medications, then use gargles and mouthwashes that cleanse the brain for many days beforehand, along with improving his diet.
Then shave his head, then cauterize one burning in the center of the head as previously described in the method, and another burning at the back. And on each temple of his head, one burning. If the patient is strong and can tolerate it, cauterize the burnings mentioned for paralysis and bodily weakness on the vertebrae of the neck and back, and the cautery iron should be olive-shaped as previously described.
If the patient is a child, make the cautery iron mild in this form.
Chapter Eleven.
On Treating Melancholia.
If the cause of melancholia is corrupt humors and thick phlegm, apply the cauterizations we mentioned in the treatment of paralysis.
If the cause of melancholia is an excess inclined towards blackness and the body of the patient is moist, give him what purifies his brain as was mentioned earlier in the classification.
Then shave the patient's head, then make a solid cake from linen like a circle, then place it in the center of his head while the patient is sitting cross-legged holding it on all sides. Then take one pound of old sheep's fat.
Then heat it over fire to a moderate temperature, about what a finger can endure when inserted into it. Then pour it in the center of his head within the circle and leave it until it cools. Do this once a week for the patient along with other proper treatments until he recovers, if God wills.
And if you wish, cauterize it with small drops without holding the cautery iron tightly, but rather by light touches. For this type of cauterization moderately moistens the brain.
Then apply cotton soaked in sheep fat or chicken fat to it.
Chapter Twelve.
On Cauterizing Water Discharge from the Eye.
If it becomes clear to you that water is discharging from the eye based on the symptoms mentioned in the classification, then immediately give the patient what purifies his head, protect him from all moistures, and induce sweating in the bath on an empty stomach for several days.
Then shave his head and cauterize a spot in the middle of the head, then cauterize two spots on the temples if the water starts to flow from both eyes or from one side if it is from one eye.
Then cut with the cautery all the veins and arteries under the skin, and let the cauterizations be long in width on the temples, and beware of bleeding.
If you see anything of it, cut it immediately with whatever treatment is possible for you, and we will come to the wisdom in threading the arteries, cutting them, and preventing bleeding.
And it may be cauterized on the back of the head under the two bones with two significant cautery marks.
Chapter Thirteen.
On the cauterization of chronic tears.
If the tears of the eye are chronic and constant, and they come from the veins and arteries that are on the outer surface of the head, and you are certain that this is due to excessive cold and thick phlegm, then cauterize with the cautery I described precisely at the start of the water flowing. Cauterize in the middle of the head, and cauterize two spots on the temples, and two spots at the back of the head under the two bones. If more is needed, cauterize one spot on each side at the tail of the eye near the eyebrow with a small cautery iron.
Chapter Fourteen.
On the cauterization of foul-smelling nose.
If you treat it with what we mentioned in the division and the treatment does not succeed, then quickly apply the qawwaiya to the patient for three nights, then shave his head and cauterize it moderately with an olive-shaped cautery iron. Then cauterize it twice above the eyebrows slightly under the hair with a nail-shaped cautery iron, and be careful not to cut the artery. This is the image of the nail-shaped iron.
Chapter Fifteen.
On cauterizing the relaxation of the eye lid.
If the eyelid sags due to illness or moisture, cauterize the eyelid once with this crescent-shaped cautery iron.
If you wish, cauterize it slightly above the eyebrows twice on each side and keep away from the temples; the length of each cautery should be equal to the length of the eyebrow.
Do not overdo the cautery with your hand, but to the extent that a third of the skin is burned, and the shape of the cautery iron should be as described.
Chapter Sixteen.
On cauterizing the eyelid.
If the eyelashes turn inward and irritate the eye, then the cautery for this has two types. Either cauterize with fire or cauterize with a burning medicine. As for cauterizing with fire, you should instruct the patient to stop plucking his eyelashes if he does so, until they grow long and even.
For if you pluck them at the time of their growth, then bind his eyes with a bandage so that they do not move until they grow. Once they have grown and settled, place the patient's head in your lap, then mark on the eyelid with ink the shape of an as leaf.
And the beginning of the mark should be near the eyelashes, then place under the eyelid cotton soaked in egg white or in the saliva of a lizard, then heat an iron, this is its shape.
Then iron over the shape you marked little by little in many times until the surface of the skin, which is like the shape of an as leaf, is all burned, especially its outer part. A sign of the correctness of your work is to see that the eyelid has wrinkled and the hair has risen from the eye flesh.
Then raise your hand at that time and leave it for three days, then apply cotton with fat until the scab falls off, then treat it with ointment until it heals, if God wills. If any hair returns after some time and the eyelid relaxes.
Then repeat the cauterization on that area as you did at first. If the hair is in the lower eyelid, trim it until it returns to its natural position and does not touch the eye with the hair. As for cauterization with a burning medicine, instruct the patient to let the eyelashes grow long and even.
Then make a shape of an as leaf from paper. Then take from the known soap and unslaked lime, one dirham or so of each, and grind them both very well together. Do this quickly so that it does not dry out. Then spread it on the paper you have made like a leaf of basil, and place it over one or both eyelids, and put cotton soaked in egg white under the eye, and have the patient's head in your lap.
Place your index finger on the medicine and press it slightly while moving it whenever the patient feels the sting of the medicine because it will feel like fire to him. As long as he feels the sting, leave the medicine and move it with your finger. When the sting subsides, remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
And look, if you see the eyelid has risen as it does when cauterized with fire or cut, and if not, then reapply the medicine to the area where it did not affect and did not turn black until you complete your work and the eye is cauterized. Then apply cotton with fat until the inflammation of the burn subsides.
Then treat it with the palm ointment or another until it heals. You should be extremely careful during the procedure to ensure that no part of the medicine falls into the eye, for if the eyelid becomes loose after a few days, there is a fear of hair falling into the eye.
Reapply the medicine to the area of the eyelid that has become loose as you did initially, then treat it until it heals. This is a picture of a basil leaf.
Know that people's eyes differ in size, so adjust your cauterization accordingly. The right way is not hidden from one who has experience in this craft.
Chapter Seventeen.
On treating the hemorrhoid that appears in the rectum.
If you treat the hemorrhoid with what we mentioned in the divisions of diseases and your treatment is not effective, it should be cauterized according to this method.
Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap, and have a servant hold his head in your hands so that he does not move or shake his head.
Then place cotton soaked in egg white or in the saliva of a tortoise on his eyes, then heat the cautery which looks like this.
It should be hollow like the shape of a vulture feather on one end where the cautery is, and if you wish, the other end can be open, or it can be closed like a spindle, but this hollow one is better for your work, God willing.
Then squeeze the hemorrhoid if it is open and extract the pus, and dry it. If it is not open, then open it and extract its pus, then place the heated cautery on it while it is very hot, hold it with your hand until it reaches the bone.
Keep your hand slightly away from the eye towards the nose during cauterization so that your hand does not make a mistake or disturb the patient, causing the cautery to fall into the eyelid and damage it. If you reach the bone with the first application of cauterization, otherwise repeat the cautery if necessary.
Leave it for three days, then apply cotton with fat and treat it with a drying ointment until it heals. If forty days have passed and it has not healed, apply a sharp, corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed, and scrape it as will be mentioned in its section, God willing.
Another method for cauterizing the hernia mentioned by some early practitioners is to direct attention to the site of the hernia, cut it open, then place a thin tube into the incision. This is its shape.
Pour into it the amount of a drachm of molten lead, and hold the tube firmly with your hand without moving. The patient must not move at all so that the molten lead does not flow to his eye. It is advisable to place cotton soaked in egg white or water on the patient's eye.
For the lead burns the site of the hernia and cures it remarkably. If the hernia is cured by the cauterization and treatment mentioned, then there is no need for further action; otherwise, it is necessary to use nasal piercing and return the hernia to the nasal passage as will be detailed in the section specifically addressing this procedure.
Chapter Eighteen.
On cauterizing the cleft lip.
A cleft often occurs in the lip, called a fissure, especially in the lips of children, as it frequently happens. If you treat this cleft with the method mentioned in the division and the treatment is not effective, then heat a small scalpel cautery in this form.
Its interior should be thin like a knife. Then place it, while hot, quickly into the cleft until the cauterization reaches the depth of the fissure. Then treat it with kerotini until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Nineteen.
On treating the abscess occurring in the mouth.
If a swelling appears at the root of the gums or in the palate or at the roots of the molars, then it hardens and bursts, and the pus that flows from it forms an abscess, and if you treat it but the treatment is ineffective, you should heat an iron to fit the size of the abscess.
Then, insert it while hot into the abscess hole and hold your hand until the iron reaches the depth of it. Do this once or twice, then treat it with the treatments we have mentioned until it heals, if God wills.
If the material is severed and it heals, well and good; otherwise, it is necessary to examine the area and remove the decayed bone as will be detailed in its respective section, if God wills.
Chapter Twenty.
On treating loose teeth and gums.
If the gums become loose due to moisture and the teeth move, and treating them with medications is ineffective, place the patient's head on your lap, then heat the iron, whose image will come after this, and place a tube on the tooth.
Insert the heated iron quickly into it and hold your hand for a moment until the patient feels the heat has reached the root of the tooth, then raise your hand. Repeat this with the iron as many times as you deem necessary, then have the patient rinse their mouth with salt water.
Hold it for an hour and then remove it. The loose tooth will become stable, the relaxed gums will tighten, and the harmful moisture will dry up.
Chapter Twenty-one.
On the Pain of the Tooth.
If the toothache is due to cold or there is decay in it and treatment with medicines has not been effective, then cauterization can be done in two ways: either by cauterization with fat or by cauterization with fire.
As for cauterization with fat, it involves taking buffalo fat, heating it in an iron spoon or shell, then wrapping cotton around the tip of a probe and dipping it in the heated fat. You then place it quickly on the painful tooth and hold it until it cools.
Then repeat this several times until the heat reaches the root of the tooth. If you prefer, you can dip a piece of wool or cotton in cold fat and place it on the painful tooth, then put a heated iron above it until the heat reaches the bottom of the tooth.
As for cauterization with fire, you should take a copper or iron tube that is somewhat thick to prevent the heat of the fire from reaching the patient's mouth. Then heat the cautery tool, whose image is provided, and place it directly on the tooth. Hold it until the cautery tool cools down. Repeat this several times.
The pain will be gone either that same day or the next day. After the cauterization, the patient should fill their mouth with good fat, hold it for a while, and then spit it out. This is the image of the cautery tool.
Cauterize with whichever end you prefer and to the extent possible. This is the image of the tube.
Chapter Twenty-two.
On castrating pigs.
If the pigs suffer from phlegm and cold humidities and do not mature with medicines, and you want quick maturity, heat the hollow iron, which has its ends perforated as shown in this figure.
So that the smoke comes out from the other end when cauterizing, place it heated on the same swelling once and twice if needed until you reach the depth of the swelling. If the swelling is small, make the iron according to the size of the swelling.
Then leave it for three days and apply cotton soaked in butter until the burned part is healed, then treat it with ointment and poultices until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Twenty-three.
On cauterization for hoarseness of voice and shortness of breath.
If humidities overwhelm the windpipe, especially if this is accompanied by a cold temperament, it is advisable to first purge the patient with laxative medicines, then cauterize him at the notch of the neck near the base of the pharynx in the lower area.
Be careful not to reach the pharynx with the cauterization and do not burn more than half of the skin, then cauterize another spot at the joint of the neck at the last prominent vertebra. The cautery iron should be awl-shaped as previously described.
Then treat it with what was previously mentioned until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Twenty-Four.
On Treating Lung Disease and Cough.
If the cough and lung disease are due to cold moisture and there is no fever or consumption in the patient, and the disease is chronic, then apply two poultices above the collarbones in the low, soft, empty areas, and another poultice in the center of the chest between the breasts.
The poultice should be nail-shaped as previously described. If you prefer, your treatment may be by dripping with a poultice called the "dropper," whose form was previously described in treating ear pain, and the number of drips should be around thirty or so.
Then treat it with what was previously mentioned until it heals. You may also make a poultice with three prongs in this shape, and use it for quick cauterization because you can apply three cauteries at once with it. This is the shape of the poultice.
Chapter Twenty-Five.
On Cauterizing the Armpit.
If the head of the humerus dislocates due to slippery moisture or if it does not stay in place when reduced, making dislocation a habitual occurrence that happens with the slightest movement as we have observed, then the first thing to do is to reduce the joint. Then the patient should lie on their back or on the correct side. Then raise the skin inside the armpit upwards with the fingers of your left hand if the joint dislocated inward.
Then heat the iron with two handles which looks like this.
Then iron the skin until it penetrates to the other side and the shape of the ironing becomes four irons, and sometimes it is ironed with an iron having three points then the shape of the ironing becomes six irons and the points are according to the thinness of the material.
And this is the image of the iron with three points.
And one may be added to this number so the irons become eight, then apply the balls ground with salt to the ironing, and the patient must rest without moving the limb for a time until it strengthens, and if the dislocation is upwards, which rarely happens.
So iron above the shoulder one strong nail-shaped iron or many dotted irons, for the joint will strengthen, moisture will disappear, and the patient will heal.
Chapter Twenty-Six.
On ironing the stomach.
If cold and excessive moisture occur in the stomach, causing it to deviate from its temperament and increasing the secretions, and if various treatments have been ineffective, then the patient should lie on his back, extend his legs and arms, and be ironed with three irons. One iron under the nipple, the size of a finger, with a nail-shaped iron, and two irons below on both sides of the single iron so that the shape of the irons forms a triangle, keeping them apart to prevent them from meeting if they discharge, and the depth of the ironing should be two-thirds the thickness of the skin, and this is the shape of the irons.
In this manner and to this extent, no more.
And if you want, make one large branding in the middle of the stomach as follows.
The iron used for this single branding should be circular in shape as follows.
The stomach may be branded with dots for those who fear this branding. This is done by marking the stomach with dots using ink to the extent you desire, then branding it with a dotted iron, and then treating it with the previously mentioned treatment until it heals.
Chapter Twenty-Seven.
On branding the cold liver.
If pain in the liver is due to cold and moisture or to a heated vapor such that it has departed from its natural temperament excessively, and if the patient has been treated with what we mentioned in the division but this was ineffective. It is advisable that the patient lie on their back, and three brandings should be marked with ink in this shape and exactly this quantity on the liver, below the ribs where the arm of a person ends.
There should be the thickness of a finger between each branding, and the branding should be along the length of the body in a straight line. Do not press your hand too tightly on the iron.
The heat should be such that it burns only half the thickness of the skin, no more. The patient should stand on their feet; if they cannot stand, they should lie down with their legs extended and arms raised. This is the shape of the iron.
You can cauterize these burns with a knife-shaped iron if you have the skill and caution to do so, taking care not to over-cauterize and thus burn all of the skin, which could lead to burning the abdomen and reaching the intestines, as the skin there is thin; be aware of this.
Chapter Twenty-Eight.
On cauterizing the swelling of the liver.
If there is an abscess in the liver and you want to determine whether the swelling is in the liver's flesh or its membrane, know that if it is in the liver's flesh, the patient will feel a heavy pain without sharpness.
If it is in the liver's membrane, there will be a sharp severe pain. I have observed that physicians find its treatment challenging. The patient should lie on their back, and then you should apply a poultice to the swollen area.
Then heat the iron in the fire, which is the iron that resembles a chisel, and this is its shape. Cauterize it once with it until you burn all the skin and continue cauterizing until you reach the membrane, causing all the pus to come out. Then treat it as you would an abscess until it heals.
This type of cauterization should only be performed by someone who has long practiced medicine and has extensively treated these diseases through experience. In that case, they may undertake such a procedure, though I consider leaving it to them the best option.
Chapter Twenty-Nine.
On stitching the wound.
The early ones mentioned cauterization with the roots of the zeraunud for a cold wound in this manner: take one root from the dry long zeraunud roots, as long as you can find, and it should be as thick as a finger. Then dip it in oil and ignite it in fire. Then cauterize with one large cautery between the connection of the clavicle and the neck, two small cauteries slightly below the carotid arteries, leaning towards the side under the beard, and two large cauteries above the breasts, between the third and fourth ribs.
Two more cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, leaning slightly backward. Another cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. Three cauteries from behind: one between the shoulders, and two beside the spine below the cautery that is between the palms.
You should not plunge your hand deep with the cautery but it should be on the surface of the skin slightly. Some of the early ones mentioned that some people used an iron cautery resembling a nail, heating it and inserting it between the ribs until it reaches the swelling itself.
The fluid is discharged as we mentioned in the swelling of the liver. With this cautery in the belly, there is a risk that either the patient may die immediately or an Fistula may develop in the area which cannot be cured.
Chapter Thirty.
On cauterizing the spleen.
If you treat the spleen disease with the treatments we mentioned in the division and your treatment is not effective, then cauterization can be done in three ways, all of which are correct. One of them is to cauterize it with three or four cauteries arranged along the length of the spleen.
In the form of liver cauterizations which are presented in their shape, and there should be between each cauterization the thickness of a finger or slightly more. The quality of the cautery is as we mentioned for liver cauterization, and you should not deepen too much with the cautery. The patient is laid on his back.
And the other side is in the elbow, lift the skin opposite the spleen where the patient's left elbow ends, and lifting the skin should be across the body so that the cauterizations fall along the length of the body.
Then insert the two probes very carefully until they penetrate the skin on the other side, then remove the cautery so that there are four cauterizations. If you wish, you can use the other cautery with three probes.
Then treat the cauterized area after allowing it to discharge pus for many days, as this is more effective than all the previous treatments mentioned.
Chapter Thirty-One.
On the cauterization for dropsy.
Cauterization is only beneficial for dropsy of the dry type, specifically. If you have treated the patient with various treatments as mentioned in the classification and your treatment has not been effective, it is advisable to perform four cauterizations around the navel and one cauterization on the stomach.
Another cauterization on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind his back between the ribs, one opposite his chest, and another opposite his stomach. The depth of the cauterization should be close to the thickness of the skin. Then leave the cauterized area open to discharge pus for a long time.
Do not abandon the patient from treatment after cauterization with what is appropriate, as it combines both meanings and speeds up recovery. The shape of the iron used for cauterizing the back should be nail-shaped as previously described, and that used for the back should be olive-shaped.
Chapter Thirty-Two.
On Cauterizing the Feet and Legs.
If they swell in the case of dropsy and are filled with yellow water, it is appropriate to cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the fourth toe.
Hold the cauterizing iron with your hand and do not bend it, then raise your hand and do not return it at all, for the yellow water will drain. The cauterizing iron should be in this shape.
Then cauterize both legs, twice on each leg. The cauterization should be done with the blade-like end of the iron, along the length of the legâ€”once below the knee and another lower towards the middle of the leg. On each thigh, do two cauterizations as well.
Leave the cauterization open without treatment for a long time, allowing the water to drain from it. Then treat it with all the methods we have mentioned.
Chapter Thirty-Three.
On Cauterizing Diarrhea.
If the diarrhea is caused by cold and moisture, weakening the digestive and binding powers in the stomach and intestines, and if it has not been cured with various treatments, and you see that the patient can tolerate cauterization and is strong enough, then cauterize them with a large cauterization on their stomach. As mentioned previously regarding ironing the stomach with a circular iron and four ironings around the navel, gently use the fine nail iron and apply one ironing on cotton above the anus, either large or two.
If you see that the moistures are abundant and the patient can tolerate that, then apply one ironing on the pubic area, one on each side of the waist, and sometimes add two small ironings on the stomach near the large one. Indeed, this is a successful treatment whose benefit does not fail, if God wills.
Chapter Thirty-Four.
On ironing hemorrhoids of the anus.
If there are chronic hemorrhoids, whether many or one, and they are of thick cold mixtures or corrupted moistures, and have been treated with what we mentioned in the division but the treatment was ineffective, then apply three ironings to the patient below the sacral vertebrae slightly under the crease, in a triangular shape.
Apply one ironing below the navel, about two fingers wide. If you determine that his stomach has become cold and his food is not digesting, and you see his face swollen, then apply a large ironing on his stomach as previously mentioned, and one on his liver. Apply another one on his spleen with a nail iron, and leave the ironing open for a while, then treat him until he recovers, if God wills.
Chapter Thirty-Five.
On ironing warts.
After cutting it, if the wart is cut off, heat the iron that resembles a mill, then insert it hot into the very center of the cut wart and push your hand until the iron reaches the mouth of the vein from which the blood flows. Do this once or twice.
If the warts are numerous, cauterize each one as described, then treat them with appropriate ointments until they heal. Cauterizing them again over cotton can be more beneficial.
Chapter Thirty-Six.
On cauterizing the fistula that occurs in the anus and its surrounding areas.
If the patient does not respond to incision and the procedure we described in its place and is reluctant to do so, it may heal by cauterization. If one develops a fistula and pus and corrupt moisture flow from it over time, the first thing you should do is measure it with a thin probe.
Then determine its depth with the probe. Heat the iron that resembles a mill, then insert it hot into the fistula straight to the depth where the probe entered. Repeat the cauterization until all the corrupt substances are burned, once or twice or three times as needed.
Be careful not to burn a nerve if there is one, or a major vein. If the fistula leads to the bladder or the intestines, be cautious.
Be careful with all these areas. You should do this if the fistula is in a fleshy area and you determine that it is not penetrable. Then treat the area until it heals. If the area seals and the discharge stops and remains so for a period of time, know that it has healed completely.
And if the materials do not cease from it, know that it is penetrable or there is rotten bone in its depth or something like what will be mentioned in its place.
Chapter Thirty-Seven.
On the Treatment of the Kidneys.
If pain occurs in the kidney due to cold or heavy wind and the patient's sexual function is impaired because of that, it should be cauterized on both sides directly on each kidney with a nail cautery as previously mentioned. Sometimes it may be cauterized a third time on the same day, so there are three cauterizations in a row, which is more beneficial.
Chapter Thirty-Eight.
On the Cauterization of the Bladder.
If weakness and relaxation occur in the bladder due to cold and humidity, causing the patient to be unable to retain urine, cauterize it with a cautery below the navel on the bladder where pubic hair begins, and another cautery to the right of the navel and another to the left.
The cautery should be applied on each side to the width of a thumb joint, and it should be cauterized with one cautery below the lower back or two if necessary, using a nail cautery as previously mentioned.
Chapter Thirty-Nine.
On the Cauterization of the Womb.
If cold and humidity cause a condition in the womb that prevents pregnancy, impair its function, or cause pain upon menstruation, it should be cauterized with three cauteries around the navel as mentioned in the cauterization of the bladder. Sealing with pitch on the cotton under the back or two sealings and the iron should be nail-shaped.
Chapter Forty.
On how to dislocate the hip.
Moisture errors may affect the hip joint, causing it to dislocate from its position. Its sign is that one leg appears longer than the other when comparing them, and you will find an empty space where the dislocation occurred. It should be treated by applying a circular-like branding directly on the affected hip area.
After marking with ink around the joint, as it circles, to place the center of the circle on the joint itself. The iron used should be similar to the one shown for branding the stomach. If you do not have this iron, use the large olive-shaped iron to brand three times.
Make the branding deep according to the thickness of the entire skin, then treat it until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Forty-One.
On branding for sciatica.
If pain occurs in the hip joint and this is caused by cold and moisture, and if the treatment mentioned in the division has not been effective and the condition persists, it should be treated with laxatives such as black seed or senna seeds, or similar remedies.
Then brand it, and there are two methods of branding: either branding with cauterizing medicines or branding with fire. Branding with fire can be done in various ways, one of which is to brand three triangular burns directly on the hip joint itself, like this.
It becomes of suitable depth, and there should be between each cauterization the thickness of a finger. The cautery iron is olive-shaped; sometimes one cauterization is made in the middle at the hipbone itself. There are thus four cauterizations, or if you wish, use the circle previously described for dislocated hip, with a single cauterization.
To have the circle surround all of the hip and burn through the thickness of the skin entirely. This is the description of the cauterization for sciatica if the pain is confined to the hip itself and does not extend to the thigh and leg.
If it extends to the thigh and leg, cauterize with two cauterizations on the thigh in the place where the patient indicates the pain is felt, and one cauterization above the ankle by four fingers towards the outer side slightly. The cautery iron should be knife-shaped, and the depth of the cauterization should be only as thick as the skin.
If he indicates that the pain extends toward the toes, cauterize where he points with a pinpoint cautery iron three or four times, or more if needed. If he indicates the pain is below the knee towards the leg, cauterize there once with a knife-shaped cautery iron.
Be cautious in all your cauterizations to not burn a nerve or a major artery, as this could cause a severe or permanent injury to the patient.
I have seen cases where cauterization above the ankle was excessive, leading to gangrene in the leg that spread to the foot, causing it to become ulcerated and resulting in the corruption of the entire limb, followed by diarrhea and death. If the pain is on both sides, cauterize them in the same manner described.
Some of the wise scholars have mentioned in hip cauterization, its description is as follows: a vessel-like object is made from iron, its diameter being half a shibr, and at its mouth it is thick like a date pit or slightly less. Inside this vessel there is another vessel and a third one.
And there should be the width of a thumb joint between each vessel. The vessels are open on both sides and their height is about one or two joints. A handle made of iron, firmly attached to the vessels, is prepared for them and this is its form.
Then it is heated in the fire until it turns red and spits sparks. It is then placed on the hip of the patient who lies on his healthy side, and it cauterizes it with three circular burns at once. Then it leaves it for three days and bandages it with fat, leaving the wound open for some days.
Then treat it with ointment until it heals. The author of this book says: We rarely use this type of cauterization due to its ugliness and the terror of its appearance, and because few can tolerate it. However, it is a good form of cauterization for those who can endure it and apply it correctly.
As for cauterization with burning medicines, it involves making two vessels like rings into which the tip of the penis can fit, made of brass or iron.
There should be a height of about two joints or so around them, and the distance between them should be the thickness of a finger. They should be open at both the bottom and the top, and they should be held together in this manner.
Then place it on the true hip with the patient lying on his healthy side, and firmly grasp with your hand. Then pour between the two circles some sharp water that has been warmed by fire slightly and let it stay for about an hour; the patient should endure its stinging and burning, for he will feel a sting like fire.
Until the stinging subsides, then raise your hand with the instrument and wash all the hip with fresh water, then leave it for three days and apply fat to it until the blackness of the burn disappears. Leave it for some days until pus flows from it, for this is more beneficial.
Then treat it with ointments until it heals. If the pain extends to the thigh or leg, make a compress for him in what holds water according to how you made for the hip equally. This is the description of sharp water and I have confirmed it in the article on drug preparation.
Take equal parts of calcined salt and unslaked lime, crush them, and place them in a new pot that has one small hole at the bottom, just large enough for the mercury to enter. Place another glass pot underneath the bottom of the pot.
Then pour fresh water over the calcined salt and lime until it covers them by a finger's depth after you have firmly pressed them with your hand. Leave the pot until the sharp water drips into the bottom glass pot. Then collect all of that water and pour it over another batch of lime and calcined salt, also renewed.
It is then extremely sharp and can be used for many medical procedures and for cauterizing other body parts, as it acts like fire itself. Some medications are also used to cauterize the hip, such as turpeth mineral, balador honey, lime with soap, all pounded together.
Galen reported a story about an ancient man's treatment for hip pain and sciatica, greatly exaggerating its importance, claiming that it does not require any other treatment and that it cures in one go.
To the extent that he might enter the bath carried and come out healed. This is by taking green mercury, and if green is not available, then take fresh dry [mercury] and finely grind it with some fat, then apply it to the hip where the pain is, or on the leg, or on the thigh.
It is tightened and left for about three hours or until the patient feels that the burning has subsided. Then, he enters the bath; if his body sweats, then he is placed in the pool. The pain will go away and he will be healed by the will of God. If he is not healed, then repeat the poultice again after ten days.
For he will be healed if God wills. Know that one should not use cauterization with these medications unless the body is first purged. Dioscorides mentioned that goat dander, if used for cauterizing sciatica, is beneficial.
The cauterization should be done in this manner: take some wool, soak it in old oil, and place it on the deep area between the thumb and the wrist, which is closer to the wrist. Then, take dry goat dander.
Ignite it with fire until it becomes a ember, then place it on the wool and leave it until it extinguishes. Then take another one and continue doing this until the sensation reaches the middle of the arm to the hip, and the pain subsides by the will of God. This type of cauterization is called dander cauterization.
Chapter Forty-Two.
On treating back pain.
Pain in the back may result from various causes, such as a fall, a blow, excessive vomiting, and the like. It is due to the accumulation of cold and moist matter, and cauterization is only applied in this category alone.
When the pain is due to the accumulation of cold matter, after the patient vomits with the use of aromatic seeds and the like, cauterization should be performed on his back where the pain is located, in three rows across the width of the area itself. Mark the location with ink first, then perform five or more cauteries in each row, depending on what you judge to be within the patient's tolerance and strength.
Cauterization should be done with a point cauterizer. If you prefer, you can perform three or four cauteries with a medium-sized two-pronged cauterizer in this manner.
Chapter Fifty-Three.
On cauterizing the initial stages of hunchback.
This condition often affects small children. A sign of its initial onset in a child is difficulty breathing when standing and moving, and you may find a protruding vertebra at the end of their spine that stands out from the other vertebrae.
If you see this and wish to prevent it, cauterize it with a circular cautery in this manner. Apply the cautery evenly on each side of the vertebra. If you prefer, cauterize around the vertebra in two or three rows with a point cauterizer, making sure the points are close to each other. Then treat the area until it heals as previously mentioned.
And it is important not to use cauterization on the hump that results from nerve spasm.
Chapter Forty-Four.
On Cauterizing Gout and Joint Pains.
If the joint pains are due to cold moistures that settle in any part of the body, and if the pains occur in the legs, it is customary for physicians to call this gout, particularly.
If cold gout is treated with the various treatments we mentioned in the classification and the pains do not subside, then cauterization can alleviate them. This involves cauterizing around the joints of the legs after purging, with many cautery points. The cautery tool should be olive-shaped and medium-sized, as follows.
And if you need to apply cauterization to the foot, do so with a point cautery. If the pains rise to the knees or other joints, which often occurs, cauterize each knee with three or four cautery points on each side using the same olive-shaped cautery tool.
If more cauterization is needed, do so without deepening the cautery beyond the thickness of the skin. If the pains rise to the hips or back, apply the cauterization as we have described in the appropriate section.
If the pains are only in the hands, apply point cautery around the wrists in two rows. If the pain remains in the fingers, apply a point cautery on each joint and on the palm. If the pains rise to the elbows or shoulders after a few days.
Treat both from every side and do not let the patient lack good care and taking of medicines, for if he improves his diet and expels phlegm, then he will be cured with this cauterization, God willing.
Chapter Forty-Five.
On cauterizing fistulas.
If a hernia appears in the groin and part of the intestine and its contents descend to the testicle, and this is newly occurred and close by, it is advisable to order the patient to abstain from food for a day and to use laxatives that will expel stool from his body.
Then he should lie down in front of you on his back, and you order him to hold himself until the contents or the intestine protrude, then you push it back with your finger. Then mark with ink under the hernia on the pubic bone a sign resembling a semicircle, its ends toward the upper part of the body.
Then heat an iron that looks like this.
Until it comes white and throws sparks, then push the intestine or contents back into his body. Then have a servant place his hand on the area to prevent the intestine from protruding. The patient's legs are spread apart, and a pillow is placed under him. Another servant ties around his legs.
Another person holds his hands by placing themselves on his chest. Then lower the iron onto the same mark and press with the iron standing straight, holding it until it reaches the bone, or repeat once more if it did not reach the bone the first time.
You must protect your effort from the protrusion of the intestine while cauterizing so as not to burn it, which could result in either the death or a great disability of the patient. Know that if you do not reach the bone with the cauterization, your work will not succeed. The cautery for children should be delicate according to their size and for adults according to their size.
Then treat the cauterized area after three days with fat until the dryness from the fire disappears, then treat it with ointments until it heals. Let the patient lie on their back for forty days until the wound is sealed.
You should make his diet during the treatment such that it softens his stomach so as not to protrude the intestine when straining or defecating. Then, if he wishes to get up after forty days, use a firm bandage and keep it on for another forty days. He should reduce exertion, overeating and drinking, and loud shouting.
For if this procedure is followed, he will be completely healed, God willing. I will discuss the treatment of hernias by incision in its own section, God willing. As for a hernia that occurs elsewhere in the abdomen and is new, if you wish to prevent it from growing larger, cauterize the area with a circular cautery according to its size. Let what you burn of the skin be about two-thirds, then treat it as we have mentioned, for it will not increase, God willing. Some early practitioners have suggested cauterizing the hernia with a triangular cautery in this manner.
After you mark the hernia with ink, make a line across at the top of the hernia and another line below it. Insert your hand in the middle and use a single nail-shaped cautery. The first method of cauterization is easier and better, God willing.
Chapter Forty-Six.
On Cauterizing Ulcers.
If pain occurs in some organs due to a fall or blow and the pain persists for a long time and treatment with medicines is ineffective, it should be cauterized with a point cautery. The cauterization of each organ should be according to its size, strength, and weakness.
If the pain and ulcer persist, then if it heals from the first cauterization, well and good; otherwise, you should repeat the cautery. For these pains usually move from one organ to a neighboring one, so you should follow them with cautery until the patient is healed.
Chapter Forty-Seven.
On Cauterizing Leprosy.
As for lepers, they may greatly benefit from cautery, especially those with leprosy caused by the corruption of phlegm and black bile.
When you wish to cauterize it, if the leprosy is in its early stages and treatment with what was mentioned in the classification has not succeeded and you fear that corruption may take over the patient's entire constitution, then cauterize him on the head with five cautery applications. One in the center of the known head, the second below it toward the forehead at the end of the hair, two on the temples, and one behind on the occipital protuberance. Insert your hand slightly with the cautery so that it affects the bone a little.
And remove its scales to facilitate the breathing out of thick vapors from it and cauterize it like the spleen as previously mentioned. And if leprosy has persisted in the patient and clearly appeared, then these types of cauterization which we mentioned for the head should be applied. Cauterization at the tip of the nose, two cauterizations on the cheeks, two on the cervical vertebrae, six on the dorsal vertebrae, one large one on the coccyx at the end of the tailbone, another above it on the same plate, and two on the hips, one on each hip. Two on the knees, one on each knee, two on the shoulders, two on the elbows, two on the ribs of the chest, cauterization on every joint of his fingers and toes one cauterization, and on each heel and wrist of his hands.
And be careful of the nerve at the back of the heels so as not to burn them. Cauterization may also be done on the pubic bone, another on the mouth of the stomach, and another on the liver. Know that the more you increase cauterization, the more beneficial and effective it is.
And know that the patient does not feel pain from cauterization as a healthy person would, because his body has become numb. The size of the cautery should be adjusted according to the parts and joints, as previously described for the characteristics of the instruments.
Then treat the cauterization with crushed almond flour mixed with honey and other treatments until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Forty-Eight.
In cauterizing numbness, when a body part becomes numb and is treated with medicines, ointments, and dressings but does not heal, then cauterize the numbed body part itself according to whether the part is large or small, and let your cauterization be somewhat deeper in the thickness of the skin.
Then treat it with ointment until it heals. Cauterization may also be applied to some forms of numbness that affect the hands and feet due to issues in the vertebrae where the nerves that move that body part emerge, which can eliminate the numbness.
None but those who are knowledgeable about the anatomy of body parts and the emergence points of the nerves that move the body should undertake this.
Chapter Forty-Nine.
On cauterizing leprosy.
If leprosy persists and no medical treatment is effective, then apply cauterization to it with a slight depth according to the thickness of the skin until the whiteness disappears and its color changes.
Then treat it with ground lentils mixed with rose oil, mint leaves, and pigeon blood or the blood of doves, using an equal part of each. Mix everything together and apply it to a cloth, which should be kept on the affected area until it heals.
Chapter Fifty.
On cauterizing cancer.
If the cancer is in its early stages and you want to stop its progression, cauterize around it in a circular motion with a circular cauterizer. Some wise men have mentioned that a deep cauterization should be applied to its center, but I do not agree with this because I expect it may cause ulceration, which I have observed on several occasions.
The correct thing is to cauterize around it in a circle as we said or with many cautery points.
Chapter Fifty-One.
On cauterizing the hernia.
If a hernia occurs in someone and it delays in maturing, either due to the influential excess causing it, or because of the age of the patient if he is an old person with little blood, or due to time, and you want to hasten the maturity of the hernia, then cauterize around it with many small cautery points drop by drop.
Then leave it, for it will hasten to mature. If you want to cauterize its base, heat the cautery instrument which has this shape.
And place it in the center of the hernia until it penetrates the skin. Let the cautery be on the lower part to facilitate the flow of pus. Then treat it as appropriate until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-Two.
On cauterizing the ulcer.
An ulcer is corruption that spreads in the organ, consuming it like fire consumes dry wood. If you see an ulcer in a place that can tolerate cauterization with fire, heat many nail-like cautery instruments, small and large, according to what is suitable for the location of the ulcer.
Then cauterize it from all sides until all the corruption is completely removed and nothing remains of it at all. Then leave it for three days, and apply powdered sulfur with oil to the cauterized areas until all the scab and all the corruption fall off entirely.
Then treat it with poultices that promote flesh growth. If you see after three days that the flesh grows properly without any corruption, otherwise repeat cauterization on the remaining corrupted areas. The corroded area can be treated with sharp medicine.
For it serves as a substitute for fire with quicker benefit. I have mentioned its treatment with sharp medicine in the division, so take it from there whenever you need it.
Chapter Fifty-Three.
On the cauterization of reversed and non-reversed nails.
This condition often occurs on the soles of the feet, and it is a rough thing that bothers the person. Cauterization in this case can be done in two ways: either by fire cauterization or by cauterization with sharp water.
As for cauterization by fire, it involves heating a hollow iron tool similar to an eagle's feather. The tool should be made of iron and sized to fit around the nail on all sides, with a thin edge. Then, place the heated tool directly over the nail and rotate your hand with the tool around the nail until the tool reaches the depth of the nail.
Leave it for three days to pus, then dress it with crushed wild barley mixed with salt and leave the dressing on it overnight, as it will remove it from its roots. Then treat the wound site with a flesh-growing ointment until it heals. If the nails are not reversed.
And this often occurs on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and legs. You should take a tube made of copper or iron or similar to an eagle's feather, place it over the nail or wart, then pour a small amount of sharp water into the tube.
Hold your hand as you turn it with a slight twitch of your hand so that the edge of the tube affects the base of the nail, and the sharp water finds its way to penetrate to the base of the nail, and the patient endures the sting of the sharp water for a moment.
Then leave it, for the nail will be extracted with its root. Do this one by one until you have treated all of them in the body. Then treat the areas after extraction with ointments that promote flesh growth.
Chapter Fifty-Four.
On cauterizing the nasal polyps.
If one develops nasal polyps due to cold in the nerve or from quartan fever or otherwise, it is advisable to cauterize them four or five times between the vertebrae, with a cautery at each vertebra, and a cautery on his chest. And on his stomach, apply a cautery with an olive-shaped iron, for the nasal polyps will subside and hasten the maturation of the cold disease.
Chapter Fifty-Five.
On cauterizing boils that occur on the body.
Boils may appear on the body, formed from cold, thick, putrid materials. When they first appear, each boil should be cauterized gently at its top with a heated cautery, such as a lit end of an iron rod, or the long root of zeraunjan (a type of metal), or with a lentil-shaped cautery iron.
And the abscesses may be cauterized at the beginning of their outbreak in this manner, so they do not increase and the effective excess dissipates, and the sick person recovers from it, except that this should be after the sick person has been purged by venesection.
Chapter Fifty-Six.
On cauterizing bleeding occurring from cutting an artery.
Bleeding of blood often occurs from a severed artery in an external wound or when incising a tumor or cauterizing an organ and the like, making it difficult to cut it.
If this happens to someone, quickly put your index finger on the mouth of the artery and hold it tightly until the blood is contained under your finger and nothing comes out. Then place several small and large olive cauters in the fire and blow on them until they become very hot.
Then take one, either small or large, depending on the wound and the place where the artery was severed. Place the cauterization tool directly on the vein after quickly removing your finger and hold it until the bleeding stops.
If the blood gushes out when you remove your finger from the mouth of the artery and extinguishes the cauterization tool, quickly take another one from those in the prepared fire. Continue doing this with one after another until the bleeding stops.
Be cautious not to burn a nerve, which could cause another disability in the patient. Know that if blood is bleeding from an artery, it cannot be cut, especially if the artery is large, except by one of four methods: either by cauterization as we said, or by amputation if it has not already separated. For if it is amputated, its ends will contract and the blood flow will cease. It can be tied tightly with threads, or medicines that stop the bleeding and tighten with bandages can be applied firmly.
As for those who attempt to cut it with a ligature or by tightening with cloth or placing cauterizing substances and the like, it will not be severed at all except rarely. If such a thing occurs to someone and there is no doctor or medicine available, they should immediately place the index finger on the mouth of the wound itself as we have described.
It should be tightened greatly until the blood is constricted and flows out above the wound and on the artery. The finger should not be removed, always keeping it cool with very cold water until the blood freezes, thickens, and stops. During this time, assess what cautery or medicine might be needed.
The Second Chapter.
On Incisions, Punctures, Lancing, Surgical Operations, and the Like.
Khalef said, we have mentioned in the first chapter every disease that can be treated with cauterization by fire and burning medicines, their causes, reasons, instruments, and forms of cautery tools. I have arranged this from head to foot in sections.
And I will follow the same approach in this chapter to make it easier for the student to understand what is required.
Before I begin, you should know, my sons, that this chapter contains more risks than what is in the first chapter on cauterization.
And for that reason, the warning should be stronger because the work in this field often results in excessive bleeding which sustains life when opening a vein or incising a swelling or lancing an abscess or treating surgery or extracting an arrow or incising on a stone and other similar procedures which all accompany risk and fear and often result in death.
And I advise you to avoid what is doubtful for you, for various kinds of people with different diseases may come to you in this profession. Some of them may be weary from their illness and may have given up hope, considering death lightly.
Due to the severity of his illness and the prolongation of his suffering, there are signs of impending death in his disease. Some may spend all their wealth on you, hoping for health, but their illness is relentless. Therefore, you should not be influenced by those who come to you with such characteristics at all.
Let your caution be greater than your desire and eagerness, and do not proceed with anything unless you have certain knowledge that is valid to you regarding the desirable outcome. Use your knowledge and warn in all treatments of your patients about what leads to safety.
For in that, you will find support in acquiring praise, glory, remembrance, and commendation. May God guide you to wisdom, O my sons, and not deprive you of the right and success. Indeed, that is in His hand; there is no god but He.
I have arranged this chapter in sections following what was mentioned earlier in the chapter on cauterization, from the ankle to the foot, to make it easier for you to find what you need from it, if God wills.
The first chapter.
On the treatment of water that accumulates in the heads of children.
This disease often affects children at birth if the midwife presses the child's head without gentleness, and it may also result from a hidden illness that is not known.
I have not seen this illness in anyone other than children, and all of those I have seen from them died quickly, which is why I decided to avoid treating it. I have indeed seen a child whose head was filled with water, and the head grew larger each day. Until the child could not even sit up due to the enlargement of his head, and the moisture increased until he perished.
This moisture either accumulates between the skin and the bone or beneath the bone on the pericranium. The procedure for this is as follows: if the moisture is between the skin and the bone and the swelling is small, it should be incised with a single transverse cut in the middle of the head, with the length of the cut about two inches so that the moisture can drain. This is the image of the surgical instrument.
If the moisture is more and the swelling is larger, make two intersecting incisions in this manner:.
