Chapter Sixty.
On the Extraction of Stones.
We have mentioned in the classification the types of stones and their treatment with medicines, and I have described the difference between stones formed in the kidney and those formed in the bladder, and the signs of each. I also discussed the stone that requires manual intervention and incision.
It is the stone formed specifically in the bladder, which pierces the urethra, and I will describe this with clear explanation and brevity.
I say that the stone formed in the bladder most commonly affects young boys, and one of its signs is that urine exits the bladder resembling water in its thinness.
Sand appears in it, and they scratch their penis and fidget with it. It often hangs down, spreads out, and diarrhea is common among them. Young boys are more susceptible to this until they reach fourteen years of age, while it is difficult for the elderly. As for young adults, their condition is somewhere in between.
He whose stone is larger has his treatment easier, and the small ones are the opposite. So when we come to treat, it should first be that the patient is given an enema that expels all the waste in his intestines, for its presence may hinder the discovery of the stone.
Then take the patient by his legs, shake him downwards to make the stone descend to the neck of the bladder, or have him jump from an elevated place several times. Then sit him in front of you upright with his hands under his thighs so that the bladder is entirely tilted downward, then examine it.
Examine it from the outside, and if you feel the stone in the space, immediately incise over it. If it does not fall under your touch at all, then you should smear the index finger with oil from the left hand if the patient is a child, or the middle finger.
If he is a full-grown boy, insert it into his anus and search for the stone until it falls under your finger. Then move it little by little to the neck of the bladder. Then press on it with your finger and push it outward toward the place where you want to make the incision.
You order a servant to compress the bladder with his hand and command another servant to lift the testicles upward with his right hand, and with his other hand to pull the skin below the testicles away from the site where the incision will be made. Then you take the lancet, which looks like this:.
You incise between the anus and the testicles, not in the middle but toward the left side. The incision should be made directly over the stone, with your finger in the anus pressing it outward so that the incision is wide on the outside and narrow on the inside to allow the stone to pass through.
There is no greater [thing] for perhaps the finger in the catheter presses the stone at the incision so it comes out without difficulty, and know that there may be some stones with angles and edges which make their exit difficult for this reason.
And there are some that are smooth like acorns and rounded, which makes their exit easy. As for those with angles and edges, you should increase the incision slightly; if it still does not come out this way, you must resort to other methods, either by grasping it firmly with a tool whose end is like an abrasive.
to secure it on the stone so that it does not slip away, or insert a delicate curved tool under it; if you cannot manage it this way, widen the incision slightly; if any blood impedes you, cut it with scissors.
If there is more than one, push the larger one towards the bladder opening first, then incise for it, then push the smaller one afterward. Do the same if there are more than two. If it is extremely large, it is unwise to make a large incision because it exposes the patient to one of two dangers.
Either the patient may die, or there will be perpetual dripping of urine because the place will not heal at all. However, try to push it out until it comes out, or resort to breaking it with forceps to remove it in pieces.
When you have finished your work, wash the wound with cedar, oak galls, and sumac, then suture it. Place a cloth soaked in oil and syrup or rose ointment and cold water on top to cool the hot swelling. Then have the patient lie on their back and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
If it dissolves, wash the area with much water and oil, then treat it with the powdered ointment and the basilicon ointment until it heals. If there is a hot swelling or corruption in the wound, such as blood clotting in the bladder and obstructing urination, this can be known from blood coming out with urine.
Insert your finger into the wound and remove that blood, for if it remains, it will lead to corruption and infection of the bladder. Then wash the wound with vinegar, water, and salt, and treat each type as appropriate until it heals.
It is advisable during all times of treatment to bind the thighs together to keep the medicines in place that are put on the area. If the stone is small and has moved into the urethra, becoming lodged there and preventing urination, treat it with what I will describe before resorting to incision.
For I have often dispensed with incision using this treatment, as I have tried it. It involves taking a probe made of steel that looks like this:.
The tip is triangular and sharp, fixed to a handle. Then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone so that it does not return to the bladder. Then gently insert the steel probe into the urethra until the tip reaches the stone itself.
Rotate the probe with your hand around the stone gradually, aiming to pierce it until you penetrate through the other side. At that moment, urine will flow out. Then press your hand on what remains of the stone from the outside of the penis; it will crumble and be expelled with the urine, and the patient will heal.
And if this treatment is not possible for you due to an obstacle hindering you from doing so, tie a thread under the stone and another thread above the stone, then incise on the stone in the same rod between the two bindings, then extract it.
Then untie the binding and clean the clotted blood that has formed in the wound. The thread is tied under the stone so that it does not return to the bladder, and the other binding above so that when the thread is untied after the stone's removal, the skin returns to its place, covering the wound.
For this reason, you should, when tying the upper thread, lift the skin upwards so that it returns to its place upon finishing and covers the wound as we have said.
Chapter Sixty-One.
On Removing Stones from Women.
Stones rarely form in women. If one of them does have a stone, treating it is difficult and often impossible for various reasons: one being that the woman may be a virgin, and another being that you may not find a woman who allows herself to be examined by a doctor.
If she is chaste or a close relative, and thirdly, you may not find a woman skilled in this craft, especially the work done by hand. The fourth reason is that the location for incision on the stone in women is far from where the stone is, thus requiring a deep incision.
This carries danger. If necessity calls for it, you should seek a skilled female doctor, though they are rarely found. If you cannot find one, then request a chaste and gentle male doctor, or have a skilled midwife present, or a woman who has some knowledge of this craft.
Prepare her and order her to do all that is commanded of her for the examination of the calculus first, which is that she should look if the woman is a virgin, it is appropriate for the finger to be inserted into her anus to search for the calculus, and if she finds it, she should press it with her finger.
Then order her to part [herself], but if she is not a virgin and is married, then order the midwife to insert her finger into the patient's vagina and search for the calculus after placing her left hand on the bladder and squeezing it well.
If she finds it, she should extract it from the mouth of the bladder downwards to the extent of her ability until she reaches the base of the thigh. Then she should make an incision opposite the middle of the vulva at the base of the thigh on whichever side is accessible and where she feels the calculus.
And her finger should not move from pressing under the calculus, and let the incision be small at first, then insert the catheter through that small incision. If she feels the calculus, she should enlarge the incision to the extent she knows the calculus can come out of. Know that there are many types of calculi.
Some are small, some large, some smooth, some rough, some long, some round, and some branched. Recognize their types to determine what you need. If the blood overpowers you, sprinkle powdered zaj in the area and hold it for a while until the bleeding stops, then continue with your work.
Until the calculus is extracted, prepare the instruments mentioned for removing calculi from men to assist you in your work. If bleeding overpowers you and you determine by the pulse of the blood that an artery has been cut, apply the cauterization to the area.
And tie it firmly with bandages and leave it without returning to it, and leave the stone without extracting it, for perhaps the patient may die. Then treat the wound; if the intensity of the bleeding subsides after days and the area becomes putrefied, return to your work until you extract the stone.
Chapter Sixty-Two.
On Incising the Watery Hydrocele.
Hydrocele is a collection of moisture in the white membrane that lies beneath the skin surrounding the testicle, which is called the scrotum. This membrane may have a special sac prepared by nature on one side of the testicle.
Until it seems as if there is another testicle. It exists between the scrotal skin and the white membrane we mentioned. This rarely occurs. This hydrocele develops due to a weakness in the testicles, leading this material to accumulate. It can also occur due to an impact on the testicles.
This moisture can have various colors; it may be yellowish, or reddish like blood, or blackish like dirt, or whitish like water, and this last is the most common. These are the signs by which it is recognized.
Where the water accumulates, if it is in the white membrane we mentioned, the swelling will be round and slightly elongated like the shape of an egg, and the testicle will not be visible because the moisture surrounds it on all sides.
If the moisture is in a special sac for it, then the swelling will be round on one side of the testicle.
For this reason, a person may imagine it to be another egg. If the moisture is between the scrotum skin and the white membrane, then it can be sensed. And if you want to know the color of the moisture, then press the swelling with the square probe whose image was previously described; judge its contents by what comes out after the probe.
When we come to treatment with iron, it is advisable to order the patient to bleed if that is possible and you see his body is full. Then he should lie on his back on something slightly elevated and put many cloths under him, then you sit on his left side.
And you order a servant to sit on his right, extending his member toward one side of the scrotum skin and towards the flank of the abdomen. Then you take a wide lancet and cut the scrotum skin lengthwise from the middle nearly to the groin.
The incision should be straight, parallel to the line that divides the scrotum skin into two halves until it reaches the white membrane containing it. You peel it back and be careful not to cut it. Your peeling should be from the side that adheres more to the testicle and you extend the peeling as much as you can.
Then you widely suture the water-filled membrane and remove all the water. Then separate the edges of the incision with forceps and pull the membrane upwards without touching the scrotal skin containing it, and cut the membrane as much as possible, either in one piece or in segments.
Especially its thin side, for if you do not cut it sufficiently, you cannot be sure that the water will not return. If the testicle protrudes out of its skin while you are working, then after you finish cutting the membrane, put it back and suture the edges of the scrotum skin together.
Then treat it as you would other surgeries until it heals. If the tumor has decayed due to another disease, it is necessary to tie the vessels in the spermatic cord for fear of bleeding, then cut the testicle from the cord and remove the tumor, then treat it as we have described.
If the collected water is in both sides, then know that they are kidneys. Incise the other side as you did with the first one. If it is suitable for you to perform the procedure in the same manner, do so, then wipe away the blood.
You insert into the incisions wool that has been dipped in oil or in rose fat, and you place outside another layer of wool that has been dipped in a mixture of juice and oil, spreading it over the testicles and the abdominal muscles, then place folded cloths on top, which are the bandages. And bind it from above with a six-terminal bandage in this manner:.
Then take two cloths, sew and stuff them with loose wool as in this example, and make the ends that need to be tied from cotton or moist wool, gather them by pulling into the waistband of the pants, and one end should go around the buttocks to the back.
The second one should be taken towards the pubic area, with the two ends on the thighs below and the remaining two ends on the buttocks, and gather all the tension into the waistband of the pants. This procedure for the kidneys can also be done by cauterization instead of incision with iron.
This involves taking a slender cauterizing tool and incising the skin of the testicle while it is hot, as described, until the white membrane containing the fluid is exposed. Then take another cauterizing tool in this manner:.
It resembles the Greek eye, then apply that membrane while it is warm until all the moisture comes out, then extend the membrane with forceps and peel it with an iron, remove the layer containing [the pus] as much as you can until you completely excise it, be careful of the ovum so that fire does not touch it.
Know that this procedure is safer and less likely to cause bleeding than incision. If during the process of incision or cautery, a hot swelling or bleeding or something else occurs, you should treat each of these occurrences with the appropriate treatment as previously described.
If the patient is timid and cannot endure this procedure due to its severity, then use the poultice as I will describe. This should be validated by you according to the evidence we have provided.
The abscess is filled with fluid, so the patient should sit on a high chair. Then, apply a broad lancet to the lower part of the swelling and place the poultice along the body. Make the opening wide enough for all the fluid to drain out, then put cotton on the area and bandage it.
Leave it to drain the remaining fluid, then treat it until the wound heals. If the fluid does not drain during the poultice application, it is likely due to a white membrane obstructing the mouth of the wound and preventing the fluid from exiting.
In that case, you should insert a goose quill or the instrument used to extract the fluid from abscesses, which was previously described, or slightly enlarge the opening of the wound.
And know that the water may return and collect after six months or so, and if it collects, treat it in the same manner, and the patient should endure his days.
Chapter Sixty-Three.
On Incising the Fleshy Adrenal Gland and Its Treatment.
Know that incising this gland is one of the dangerous procedures leading to destruction in most cases; therefore, we see it better to leave it and be safe from it. I will mention the procedures concerning it and the types of swelling.
I say that many swellings may occur in the bodies that constitute the ovaries, and this can result from various causes: either from sharp residue that flows into the ovaries or from a blow. The color of the swelling is like the color of the body, and it does not contain water.
The swelling may be soft, and sometimes the swelling is hard, its color like a mole, and it has no sensation. It can result from the entanglement and swelling of the arteries, as previously mentioned, or from the swelling of the veins. If it results from the swelling of the arteries, this can be identified by the dispersion of the swelling.
If you press it with your fingers, it should not be subjected to any cutting at all. As for that which results from the swelling of the veins, nothing will disperse when pressed with the fingers. This type may be incised along with the other flesh.
This involves incising the scrotal skin, then lifting the testicle upward and extracting it from the white membrane. You must free the spermatic cord from the vessels, tie off the vessels, and cut the spermatic cord after freeing it from all sides of the testicle. If the testicle has adhered to those growing muscles.
It is necessary to extract the cyst and cut it, and if there is adhesion between any of the peritoneal layers or between the vessels, it is necessary to completely remove all that adhesion and cut it in a circular manner.
If the flesh growth is in the adhesion site which is at the back, it is necessary to cut all of it and extract the cyst as we said. Once your work is done, wash the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and drink, then treat it with all treatments until it heals.
Chapter Sixty-Four.
On the treatment of aden in the groin.
The groin swelling is a twisted lump similar to a cluster, with relaxation of the testicles, making movement, exercise, and walking difficult for the patient. The treatment of this ailment is closely related to what has been mentioned earlier.
However, it is necessary to mention the procedure as performed by our predecessors. I say that the patient should sit on a high chair, then push the testicles downward with a scoop, and hold the skin of the testicle with your fingers along with the vessels that are close to the penis.
And a servant other than you should hold them and stretch them tightly, then cut with a wide sharp scalpel along the vessels until they are exposed. Then peel from both sides as I mentioned in the section on dissecting the arteries in the limbs, then sew them with a needle containing a doubled thread.
Tie it at the first places where the groin swelling appeared and also tie it at the end. Then, cut it in the middle with a vertical incision along the body and remove all the foul and corrupt moisture that has accumulated inside.
Then treat the wound as you would other wounds that require a period for the vessels nourishing one of the ovaries to fall off, and there is no harm in that. If all the vessels are exposed to the ovarian ligament, it is necessary to remove one of the ovaries with the vessels so that the egg does not lack nutrition. Before cutting the vessels, they wither and are no longer useful.
Chapter Sixty-Five.
On the treatment of urinary incontinence.
This incontinence occurs due to a hernia that appears in the abdominal membrane extending over the abdomen, near the inguinal regions from the abdominal cavities, causing urine to flow from that hernia into one of the ovaries.
This hernia can either be due to a tear in the abdominal membrane or its extension. These two types occur due to various causes, such as a blow, a jump, a shout, lifting something heavy, and so on. Its sign, if it is due to the extension of the abdominal membrane, is that it occurs gradually over a long period of time.
It does not happen suddenly, and the swelling is flat to a certain depth because the abdominal membrane compresses the urine. Its sign, if it is due to a tear in the abdominal membrane, is that it causes severe pain immediately from the beginning, and the swelling appears differently under the skin, close by.
This occurs when urine exits and moves outside the abdominal membrane, and sometimes pus may come out with the urine. This type of incontinence is called urinary and purulent, and it can also occur with gas. Sometimes feces may flow into the urine and get stuck there, leading to the patient's death.
For it causes severe pain and rumbling, especially if squeezed. The treatment of these types of ailments with iron is dangerous so you should be wary of it. The method is to order the patient to return the excrement with his hand into his body if returning is possible.
Then he lies on his back before you and raises his legs. Then stretch the skin next to the scrotum upwards, and cut the skin of the testicles entirely lengthwise, then sew the edges of the incision with sutures as needed to open the incision.
The incision should be large enough for the egg to come out. Then peel off the membranes under the skin of the testicle until the hard white membrane is exposed on both sides. At that point, insert your index finger next to the egg.
Between the white membrane under the egg's skin and the second membrane, release the adhesion behind the egg. Then fold it with your right hand inside the scrotal skin, while at the same time stretching the white membrane upwards with your left hand and lifting the egg with the membrane to the side of the incision.
You order the servant to lift the egg upwards, and you completely release the adhesion from behind. Check with your finger to ensure there is no twisted intestine in the hard white membrane; if you find any, push it down into the abdomen below.
Then take a needle with a thick thread that is made from ten threads, and insert it at the end of the membrane under the scrotal skin that is next to the incision. Then cut the ends of the twisted thread until there are four threads. Then arrange some of them on each other in a stiff form and bind with it the peritoneum which we said is under the scrotal skin tightly from both sides, then also wrap the ends of the threads and tie them tightly so that nothing of the vessels which nourish them can reach them. So that a hot swelling does not occur and also becomes a second binding emerging from the first binding, away from it less than two fingers, and after these two bindings, leave of the peritoneum which is under the scrotal skin the amount of a finger bone.
So that a hot swelling does not occur and also becomes a second binding emerging from the first binding, away from it less than two fingers, and after these two bindings, leave of the peritoneum which is under the scrotal skin the amount of a finger bone. And all of the remaining part is cut around, and the testicle is removed with it, then a slit is made below the scrotal skin from which blood flows as we described earlier, then use wool soaked in oil and place it in the wound, and use the binding as we described.
And the white peritoneum that we mentioned after cutting it may be cauterized to prevent bleeding, as this often occurs. The binding is left until it falls off by itself; if its falling off is delayed, wash it with hot water and apply something that causes sweating until it falls off.
Then treat the wound with the rest of the treatments for wounds until it heals.
Chapter Sixty-Six.
On Hydrocele This air-containing hydrocele, I have not seen anyone dare to treat it with iron. The ancients mentioned that it should be done as we described for the hydrocele with a dartos flap, which is to tie the vessels gently below after making an incision.
Then cut in the middle and treat the swelling with what opens it until the vessels fall out, and treat the wound as mentioned until it heals.
Chapter Sixty-Seven.
On the hernia that occurs in the armpit.
A hernia may occur in the armpit as we said, where the area protrudes but nothing of the intestine descends to the arm; if it does descend, it is minimal and returns at all times.
However, if the condition persists over time, the split in the abdominal wall increases until the intestine and hernia descend into the scrotum. This occurs due to the extension of the abdominal wall that is in the armpit as we said. This is because the abdominal wall extends, then relaxes and weakens the area, causing it to protrude. Its treatment is by cauterization as I have described previously.
It can also be treated with iron in this manner: the patient lies on their back in front of you, then cut the protruding swollen hernia area transversely to about three fingers' width, then separate the abdominal walls beneath the skin.
Until the white abdominal wall beneath is exposed, then take a probe and place it on the protruding area of the abdominal wall, pressing it to the depth of the abdomen. Then sew the two protruding areas at the end of the probe on the abdominal wall together with sutures.
Then remove the probe end without cutting the abdominal wall at all, and do not touch the testicle or anything else as I informed you in the treatment of intestinal hernia. Then treat it according to the treatment of wounds.
When the threads are cut, clean them and set the wound until it heals, for the hernia retracts and does not increase the bulge.
And cauterization is better in this area because it is closer to safety.
Chapter Sixty-Eight.
On the relaxation of the scrotal skin.
The skin of the scrotum often relaxes in some people without the inner flesh relaxing, which makes its appearance unattractive. Therefore, whoever wishes to treat it should lay the patient on their back.
Cut all the relaxed skin on the thick skin, then bring the edges together. If you wish, first sew the excess relaxed skin with three or four sutures and make sure the suturing is secure, then cut what is between the sutures.
Then treat it as you would other wounds until it heals and the threads fall off.
Chapter Sixty-Nine.
On castration.
Castration is forbidden in our Sharia.
For this reason, I should not have mentioned it in this book. However, I mentioned it for two reasons: the first is so that it may be known to the physician if asked about it and to know how to treat those affected by it. The second reason is that we often need to castrate some animals for our benefit.
Like rams and bulls and cats and similar animals, I say that castration can be done in two ways, either by squeezing or by cutting. That which is done by squeezing is performed by placing the animal in hot water until its testicles relax, soften, and hang down.
Then squeeze them with your hand until they dissolve and are not noticeable upon touch. As for castration by cutting, you should hold the animal, grasp the skin of its testicles with your left hand, then tie the scrotal sacs and make one incision on each testicle.
Until the two testicles emerge, then cut them after peeling and do not leave any of the membranes on them except for the thin membrane that covers the vessels. This method of castration is better than the one done by squeezing.
Because squeezing may leave some of the testicles, causing the animal to still desire mating. Then treat the wound until it heals.
Chapter Seventy.
On the treatment of intersex conditions.
Intersex conditions in men occur in two types. The first is when a form resembling a female genitalia appears below the pubic area or on the scrotal skin between the testicles, with hair present, and urine may flow from the part on the scrotal skin.
As for women, there is one type where it appears above the vagina on the pubic hair area, resembling a small male genitalia protruding outward, one of which resembles a penis and the other two resemble testicles. The treatment for the three types.
The two types of men and the one type of women should have that excess flesh cut until its trace is removed, then treat it as you would other wounds until it heals. As for the second type of men from whom urine comes out in the skin of the testicle, there is no procedure for it nor any cure at all.
Chapter Seventy-One.
On the Removal of the Clitoris and Excess Flesh from Women's Genitals.
The clitoris may sometimes exceed the natural size until it becomes ugly and its appearance is repulsive. It may also enlarge in some women to the point that it spreads like in men and affects intercourse.
It is advisable to grasp the excess part of the clitoris with your hand or a forceps and cut it, but do not excessively cut, especially at the depth of the base, to avoid causing bleeding.
Then treat it as you would treat wounds until it heals. As for the excess flesh, it grows in the mouth of the womb until it fills it.
And sometimes it protrudes outward like a tail. For this reason, some of the early practitioners called it the tail disease. It should be cut as you would cut the clitoris, and then treat it until it heals.
Chapter Seventy-Two.
On the Treatment of Hernia.
Hernia is when the woman's vagina is not perforated or the opening is very small, which can either be natural from birth or acquired. The acquired type results from a previous condition and may be due to excess growth of flesh.
Or it is thin or thick adhesion, and it may be in the depth of the uterus or its sides or its upper part or lower part, and it prevents intercourse and conception and childbirth, and sometimes menstruation; knowledge of this is by the midwife's examination.
If the obstruction is visible and close, if it is not visible, then examine it with her fingers or a probe. If the obstruction is from thin adhesion and is close to the lips, then promptly puncture it, which means to make something like supports on the lips, then place your thumbs of both hands together.
And the woman lies on her back with her legs apart, then she stretches the lips forcefully until she punctures the thin adhesion and the obstruction opens. Then she takes wool, soaks it in oil, and places it on the area. She should have intercourse every day so that the area does not close again.
If the adhesion is thick and dense, it should be cut with a wide scalpel resembling a reed leaf. If the obstruction is from grown flesh, then grasp it with forceps and cut it. Have medicines that stop bleeding without irritation, such as scammony, psyllium, and frankincense mixed with egg white.
Then use a wide lead tube to prevent the wound from closing quickly, keep it in place for several days, and use a wick of dry linen. Then treat it with all treatments for ulceration until it heals. Sometimes other flesh growths may occur in the uterus, which should be cut out in the same manner.
Unless it is a cancerous tumor, for a cancerous tumor in the uterus should not be treated with iron at all.
Chapter Seventy-Three.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids, warts, and red boils that appear in women's genital areas.
As for hemorrhoids, it is the swelling of the ends of veins until much blood flows from them constantly. When hemorrhoids become severe, they turn into warts. I have mentioned in the classification their types and signs, and I will mention here.
What can be treated and what cannot be treated, so I say that if the hemorrhoids and warts are deep inside the uterus and do not appear to the senses, they cannot be treated with iron. What appears at the mouth of the uterus and is perceptible is what can be treated.
It is advisable that the woman enters a cool room, then stretches the warts with a probe or a coarse cloth and cuts them from their roots. Then, when bleeding occurs, apply one of the blood-stopping agents without cauterization.
Use substances like oak bark, sycamore juice, mastic, and the like. Then, raise her legs against the wall for an hour, then let them hang in cold water. If bleeding continues, sit her in a decoction of sorrel, pomegranate peel, alkanet, and the like. Then take barley flour and knead it with honey and vinegar.
Apply it to her back as a dressing; if the bleeding stops, otherwise persist with strong cupping of the veins and breasts without restriction. Then take some wool, soak it in the juice of chicory or the juice of squirting cucumber or the juice of buckthorn branches mixed with alkanet drink, and apply it to the area.
When the swelling subsides, treat the area with ointment until it heals. As for the red boil, it resembles the heads of the hÄsha, rough in appearance; it is appropriate to cut off what appears of it as mentioned regarding warts, and treat it until it heals.
Chapter Seventy-Four.
On the suppuration that occurs in the uterus.
Various types of tumors may occur in the uterus, such as cancer, hardened tumors, ulcers, debility, eating sores, polyps, hemorrhoids, fissures, warts, and hot tumors. I have mentioned all these diseases, their types, and their symptoms in the classification.
It is appropriate to mention in this article the hot tumor that occurs in the uterus, if it is one of the tumors that accumulate over a period, how its suppuration should be treated with iron. One should observe if the pain of the tumor at the beginning is sharp, accompanied by pulsation, inflammation, and fever.
And if you see that it is red and sensitive to touch, do not rush to suppurate it; treat it with what aids in ripening until these symptoms subside. Once they have subsided, the woman should then sit on a chair with two seats and lean on her back.
She should draw her legs toward the lower abdomen, with her thighs spread apart, and place her arms under her knees, securing them with a suitable binding.
For this purpose, the midwife should sit on the right side and use the instrument that opens the cervix, which will be illustrated later. If you intend to use this instrument, you should estimate with a probe the depth of the woman's uterus so that the part of the instrument inserted does not exceed the depth of the uterus.
The patient is harmed if the instrument exceeds the depth, so padding should be placed on the edge of the cervix to prevent the entire instrument from entering the depth of the womb, and the spiral that runs through the instrument should come from the upper side.
You hold the instrument and the servant turns the spiral until the cervix is opened, and when the pus appears and is felt by hand being soft and thin, you should cut it at its head with a wide scalpel, and once you have completely drained all of it.
A soft wick should be placed in the wound, soaked in rose oil or green oil that has some astringent properties. The wick should protrude from the incision in the cervix, and outside on the womb and the pubic area, clean wool soaked in water boiled with alum should be applied.
Then it should be treated after two days with the ointment suitable for that until it heals.
The womb and the wound may be washed by injecting them with water and honey, then with water in which the root of the senna or long zerafand has been boiled, then return to the ointment, if the pus is hidden inside the womb.
It should be treated without using iron but rather with what we have mentioned in the division.
Chapter Seventy-Five.
On instructing midwives how to treat live fetuses that emerge in an unnatural position.
The midwife should first know the signs of a natural birth. Among its signs are when you see the woman bending downward and longing to breathe in air, and her labor becomes easier for her.
And the fetus is quick to exit, so know that this birth will be in a natural form and it will come out head first with the afterbirth with it or hanging from its navel. If you see these signs, then you should squeeze her abdomen so that the fetus exits quickly.
For if it descends head first, the afterbirth will come with it and it will be well cleansed of those superfluous things. Any birth other than this is unnatural and blameworthy because the fetus may come out feet first or hands before its head and feet.
It may come out with one hand or one foot, or its head and a hand, or it may come out folded, or it might turn over on its back, and other blameworthy forms. The midwife should be skilled and delicate in all these matters and beware of errors and mistakes.
And I explain each of these forms and how to handle them so that you may understand and be aware. If the fetus comes out head first in a natural manner, but the woman finds it intense and labor is difficult, and you see her strength weakening, then sit her on a chair and have women hold her steady.
Bind her womb with cooked fenugreek and moist ointments, then the midwife should insert a small blade between her fingers to cut the afterbirth or tear it with her nails until the moisture inside flows out, and squeeze the woman's abdomen until the fetus descends.
If it does not descend, the woman should be infused with fenugreek juice mixed with suet. Then after the infusion, she should be ordered to strain herself and tickle her nose with cumin while holding her mouth and nose shut, for then the fetus will come out at once. If the hands of the fetus emerge first, they should be gently pushed back little by little.
If the hands cannot enter, place the woman on a stand and raise her legs upwards, then shake the stand on the ground while the woman holds on so she does not fall during the shaking. If the hands cannot enter and the fetus dies, cut them off and pull out the rest of the fetus.
Or bind his hands with a cloth and pull them gently, for it will come out. If the fetus comes out on its feet, you should push them upwards then gradually turn the fetus until it is aligned, then take one of its legs and stretch it little by little.
When they reach the thighs, order her to bear down and tickle her with cundus, for it will come out. If it does not come out as described, then gradually return the fetus until it is in its natural shape, for it will then come out smoothly. If it resists all of the above methods.
Take the saliva of the linseed, the saliva of the fenugreek, the fat of the shirjing, and dissolved gum, and pound them all together in a mortar thoroughly. Then apply it to the woman's vagina and lower abdomen. Then sit her in lukewarm water until it reaches the hips.
When you see that the lower part has softened, make her a suppository of honey and have her bear with it. If she holds the suppository for an hour, then sit her on a chair, tickle her, close her mouth and nose, and gently press her lower abdomen; the fetus will come out at that moment. If the fetus comes out on its knees and hands.
If it comes out in this manner, gradually insert your hands. Then the woman should lie on her back with her legs hanging down below while lying on a bed, clasp her hands, and gently press above her abdomen little by little. Then remove the pillows from under her legs so that the lower part is elevated. If the fetus does not come out, take both of her legs and move them with a strong motion, then squeeze above the thighs little by little until the fetus rises up, then the midwife inserts her hand and adjusts the fetus little by little.
Order the woman to strain until the fetus comes out, if the fetus comes out with one of its hands extended and stuck, try to retract the hand, if she cannot retract it then make her stand and walk, if she cannot walk then have her lie down.
Make her lie on her bed and shake her legs strongly, then use the traction device described from the levers. If labor begins, sit her on a chair, then work on retracting the hand and aligning the fetus to its normal position, make the woman sneeze and order her to strain until it comes out.
If the fetus comes out on its back, with its arms spread and its face toward its mother's back, the midwife should grasp the fetus's hand, then turn it little by little and align it gently. Once aligned, apply what we described of oil and levers to its front.
Then have her move little by little. Once she does that, sit her on the chair and order her to lean to the right side, then have her strain and make her sneeze with cinder, for it will come out, the fetus coming out standing on its side.
If it descends to the mouth of the womb in this manner with the afterbirth, cut the afterbirth with your nail until it is free from moisture. If it clings to the face and neck of the fetus, cut it from the navel so that it does not suffocate and die, then push the fetus inside until it is in the proper position.
And he ordered the woman to strain several times, for it comes out easily, like twins or many fetuses. Know that twins are often born, and three or four may be born and live, though this is rare. As for five, it is something outside of nature and they do not live at all.
And a single placenta surrounds them even if they are many, and they are separated by a membrane barrier connected to the navel of each one of them. They may come out as a single fetus does, in a natural and easy birth, or they may come out in a problematic manner as we have described.
If some of them are difficult to deliver and become in the unnatural forms we mentioned, then treat them as described. Let the midwife be gentle and do what she does with tenderness and caution, and adapt to each form with the skill that leads to safety.
What may be conceived in the womb and then abort: One, two, three, four, five, six, seven, or more than ten may be conceived. It has been confirmed to me that a woman aborted seven, and another aborted fifteen, all of them having taken form.
By the wisdom of the All-Knowing, all of this should be known to the midwife, for such situations may fall upon her one day, and she should handle them appropriately.
Chapter Sixty-Seven.
On the Extraction of a Stillborn Fetus.
If you have treated the stillborn fetus with the methods mentioned in the section on treatment, and it has not been delivered, and circumstances compel you to use manual intervention, then you should assess whether the woman is strong and does not exhibit any symptoms that could cause harm. If so, the woman should lie down on her back on a bed.
Her head should be tilted downward and her legs raised, with an attendant holding her on both sides or tying her to the bed so that her body does not shift when the fetus is pulled.
Then, she moistens the mouth of the womb with moist ointments mixed with the saliva of the linseed, fenugreek, and flaxseed. The midwife then applies these ointments and salves to her hands, gently inserts them into the womb, and seeks a place to insert the forceps for the fetus, finding suitable locations for that purpose.
If the fetus is positioned to be delivered headfirst, insert the forceps into its eyes, or at the back of its head, or in its mouth, or in its palate, or under its chin, or in the areas near the ribs, or below the floating ribs.
And if it is to be delivered feet first, then [insert the forceps] in the groin and the middle ribs. It is advisable to hold the forceps with the right hand, with its curve between the fingers of the left hand, gently insert the hand, and pierce the forceps into one of those areas we have mentioned.
Until you reach an empty space, then insert another forceps opposite it, or a third if needed, to ensure the pulling is even and does not tilt to one side. Then pull steadily, but do not pull in a straight line only; instead, move it in all directions.
To facilitate its exit, as is done with a tooth when it is extracted. In between, the pulling should be relaxed; if one part is stuck, the midwife should apply some ointment to her fingers and insert them from that side to rotate what is stuck. If part of the fetus comes out, then move the forceps to other positions.
It is raised slightly to do this until the fetus comes out entirely, but if a hand comes out first and cannot be returned due to compression, it should wrap a cloth around it then pull it until it all comes out and cut it.
Either in the wrist joint or in the elbow, and so it should be done with the other hand and the legs. If the fetus's head is large and faces difficulty in coming out or if there is water gathered in its head, you should insert a spiked forceps between the fingers.
And with it, you split the head to let out the water or crack it with an instrument called the mashdakh, whose image comes with the images of all other instruments in the chapter that follows this.
You should do the same if the fetus naturally has a large head; you should split or crush the skull with the mashdakh as mentioned, then extract the bones with forceps. If the head comes out but is compressed at the clavicle, it should be cut to allow the moisture in the chest to drain.
Then the chest will contract. If the chest does not contract and cannot come out, cut it as much as you can. If the lower abdomen is swollen or has a tumor, you should press it to let the moisture flow out.
If the fetus is in a breech position, pulling it out is easy and aligning it to the mouth of the womb is simple. If it gets compressed at the abdomen or chest, you should pull it with a cloth wrapped around your hand and cut the abdomen or chest until what's inside flows out.
If all the organs are extracted and the head recoils and is retained, then the midwife should insert her left hand; if the mouth of the womb is open, she inserts her hand into the neck of the womb and seeks the head with it and pulls it by the fingers to the mouth of the womb, then she inserts a forceps or two forceps and pulls it with them.
If the mouth of the womb has closed due to a hot swelling, it should not be forcibly treated. Instead, at this time, moist and fatty substances should be applied, dressings should be used, and sitting in water that relaxes and moisturizes is recommended.
And if the fetus is on its side, if it can be aligned, then use what we mentioned for a live fetus. If that cannot be done, then it should be cut and removed. It is necessary that nothing of the afterbirth be left inside at all. Once you are finished with the treatment, apply what we mentioned regarding the treatment of hot swellings that occur in the wombs.
If bleeding occurs, she should bathe in astringent water and use the other treatments. I have witnessed a woman who had been pregnant, and the fetus died inside her, then she became pregnant again while still carrying the dead fetus.
Then the other fetus also died. After a long time, a swelling appeared in her lower abdomen, which swelled until it burst and began to discharge pus. I was called to treat her, and I treated her for a long time, but the wound would not heal, so I applied some of the strong adhesive ointments to it.
A bone came out from the site, and after some days, another bone came out. I was amazed by this because the abdomen is a place without bones, so I estimated that they were the bones of the dead fetus. I examined the wound and extracted many bones from the fetal head.
I continued doing that until I extracted many bones from her, and the woman was in the best of conditions. She lived for a long time with some pus oozing from the place, and I only mention this rarity here.
Because it contains knowledge and assistance for what the skilled doctor attempts to treat with his hands.
Chapter Seventy-Seven.
It contains images of the tools needed for extracting the fetus.
Image of a speculum used to open the mouth of the womb:.
This clamp, with which books are leveled, has two screws at the ends of the two pieces of wood. However, this screw should be finer than the clamp and should be made either of boxwood or pine wood, and the width of each piece of wood should be the thickness of two fingers.
And their thickness is about the size of a finger, and their length is one and a half palms. In the middle of the two pieces of wood are two rods made of the same type of wood, firmly attached to them. Their length should be about half a palm or slightly more, and their width should be about two fingers or slightly more. These two rods.
These are the ones that enter the mouth of the womb to open it when you turn the screws. Image of another tool for the same purpose, finer and lighter:.
It is made from boxwood or pine wood in the shape of forceps, except that it has two rods at its end, as you see. The length of each rod is about one palm, and their width is two fingers. When you want to open the womb with it.
Sit the woman on a bed with her legs hanging down and spread apart at the knees, then insert these two guides together into the mouth of the womb while you hold the end of the instrument below between her thighs; then open your hand with the instrument as you would with forceps to the extent that you desire to open the womb. Until the midwife does what she wants, an image of another loop mentioned by the earlier authorities:.
Image of the instrument used to expel the fetus:.
Image of the instrument used to soften the head of the fetus:.
It resembles scissors with teeth at the end as you see, and it can be made rectangular like forceps as shown in this image, having teeth like a saw to cut and scrape with:.
Image of another instrument:.
Image of forceps:.
This forceps should be slightly thick so it does not break when pulling the fetus with it, image of two-pronged forceps:.
Image of two broad knives for cutting the fetus:.
All these instruments, the more their types increase and are prepared by the maker, the faster he can work and the higher his skill is regarded by people. Do not disdain any instrument from being prepared, as there may be a need for it.
Chapter Seventy-Eight.
On the Extraction of the Afterbirth.
If the afterbirth is retained after childbirth, it is necessary to instruct the patient to hold herself and then tickle her with cundus and place your hand over her mouth and nose. If it comes out by this method, otherwise take a measure.
Pierce a hole in the lid and place within it the crushed herbs that open the womb, such as fennel, thyme, aniseed, camomile, mugwort, silicium, and centaury. Use all of these medicines or some of them, immerse them in water, and carry it to the fire. Then place a silver tube on the hole of the pot lid with the other end in the mouth of the womb.
Hold it until the steam reaches the bottom of the womb, then tickle as we said, for the afterbirth will come out quickly. If it remains after this treatment and does not come out, instruct the midwife to dip her left hand in pig fat or elephant saliva.
Then insert it into the vagina and search for the afterbirth with it. If she finds it, she should grasp it and pull it out gradually. If it is attached deep in the womb, insert the hand as described until you find the afterbirth, then pull it out little by little cautiously.
So that the womb does not fall out due to strong pulling, it should be moved gently to the sides, right and left, then increase the amount of pulling, for it will respond at that time and become detached. If the mouth of the womb is closed, we have described the treatment with tickling and the pot and herbs.
If it does not come out with all that we have described, do not be forceful in attempting to pull it again. Instead, tie what has come out from it to the mouth of the womb and to the woman's thigh, then administer the quadruple ointment, for it will cause it to rot after a few days.
And it dissolves and exits, except that if it putrefies, then a foul smell rises from it to the stomach and head, which harms the patient; therefore, suitable fat should be used.
Therefore, some of the early practitioners have tried the smoke of pitch and dried figs, a picture of the machine with which the woman is vaporized when menstruation and afterbirth are retained, and so on:
It is made from lead resembling a funnel or made from copper, with the narrow end placed in the vagina and the wide end over fire. The incense prepared on hot coals is held until that incense is gone, then repeat with more.
Chapter Seventy-Nine.
On the treatment of unperforated anal fistula.
Many boys may be born with their anus unperforated, blocked by a thin membrane. The midwife should pierce this membrane with her finger, or if not, she should use a sharp lancet, being careful not to touch the muscle.
Then she places wool soaked in the decoction and oil on it, and treats it with ointments until it heals. If you fear it might close up again, place a lead tube in the opening for many days, removing it when the child needs to defecate.
The anus may also become blocked due to the healing of a wound or a swelling. It should be incised where it has healed, and then treated with the treatments we have mentioned, including the use of lead.
Chapter Eighty.
On the treatment of abscesses that occur below.
Abscesses that occur below are a complex and thickening that happens near the anus from the outside or in the space on one of the sides, and the abscess can be one or more.
If that complex persists for a long time, it opens and a white watery moisture or thin pus flows from it. Some of these abscesses may extend to the rectum and intestine, while others do not extend. The extending ones can be identified by what comes out with the stool and gas when the patient defecates.
And sometimes worms may come out of it. Some of them may be abscesses extending from the space to the bladder and the urethra, and some may extend to the hip joint and the tailbone. What distinguishes the extended abscess to the anus from the non-extended is known as well.
Insert your index finger into the anus and insert a thin probe into the abscess, made of copper or iron if there is no bend in the abscess. If there is a bend, then insert a thin lead probe or a horsehair into it.
Until you feel the probe or the hair with your finger. If you do not feel it at all, and nothing of stool, gas, or worms comes out of the opening as we said, then know that it is not extended, so proceed promptly to treatment.
If the abscess extends to the bladder or the urinary tract, the indication is urine coming out of it and its resistance to healing with medications. As for if it extends to the hip joint or the tailbone, its sign is the probe reaching that area.
If there is no deviation to the bone and the pain is in its vicinity, and pus continuously comes out of it, and no treatment works nor does it heal with ointment, these penetrating abscesses do not heal at all.
Treating them is futile labor for those ignorant doctors who attempt to treat it. As for those that are not penetrating and not chronic, there is hope for their cure with the iron as I will describe and what I have experimented with, which is to have the patient lie down in front of you on his back.
Lift his legs up and let his thighs slope towards his abdomen, then insert a copper or lead probe into the abscess if there is a deviation until you know where the probe ends. If the patient feels it near the anus, you should insert your index finger into the anus.
If you feel the probe has penetrated on its own and is exposed without sensing any membrane or flesh between your finger and it, then know for certain that it is penetrating. Do not labor over it, as it will not heal, as we have said.
It has been said that it may heal in some people, though rarely. Among the treatments that may be beneficial is to heat a thin iron on according to the size of the abscess as previously mentioned, and insert it hot into the abscess until it reaches near the anus, then repeat this two or three times.
Until you know that all the excess flesh that has formed, which resembles a bird's feather tube, has been burned off. Then treat it with a cloth soaked in fat until the burned flesh comes out. Then treat it with healing ointments; if it heals.
And if it does not heal with any other treatment ever, and if you insert the probe and it does not reach your finger which is in the fistula and there is a thick barrier of flesh or mesentery between them and you see the sinus beyond the skin surface then incise the skin from the beginning of the sinus. And you pass through the incision with the probe while it is in the sinus until the incision reaches where the end of the probe is, and the probe is removed and falls out, then clean those encrusted flesh that resembles a bird's feather tube and do not leave any of it.
Then treat it with suturing ointments until it heals. If the blood overpowers you and prevents you from completing your task of cutting that flesh, the best thing to do and what is most beneficial is to cauterize it with fire or a sharp medicine, for cauterization with fire combines two good conditions: burning off that excess flesh.
And stop the bleeding and dry out the moisture, then treat it with linen soaked in fat or sulfur powdered with oil until pus forms and the burned flesh is expelled with the pus. Then treat the wound with suturing ointments that promote the growth of strong flesh.
These are the medicines that constrict and dry. For if it heals, it is cured, and there will be no recurrence. If the sinus extends to the depth of the fistula and is far from the surface of the body, insert your finger into the fistula and explore with it.
If you feel the probe and there is a barrier of mesentery or flesh between it and you, and it is close to penetrating, then the treatment should be one of hopeful measures. This involves using one of three methods: either cauterizing it as mentioned.
And either you cut it until you reach its bottom so that you can introduce the thread and treatment closely, and do not extend the incision lest you cut the muscle surrounding the anus, causing the patient to involuntarily release excrement. Then treat him with what we mentioned, for he may be healed as we said.
And either you penetrate that membrane and pierce it after you have cut it close to the anus as we said, either with a probe or with another sharp instrument, then clean all the clotted flesh in the incision as much as you can by searching thoroughly.
Then, sew up the entire wound including the incision and the upper opening until it is sealed, leaving the fistula open inside the anus, which is less burdensome for the patient. The fistula may heal in this manner.
This is when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is on one side of the anus towards the surface of the body with the skin and the anal ring. At this point, take a probe with a perforated tip like a cobblerâ€™s needle in this manner:.
And insert a braided thread of five threads or so, then introduce the probe with the thread into the fistula until it reaches the bottom. If it penetrates the anal ring internally nearby.
Then, pull the thread out through that hole by inserting your finger into the anus and pulling out the end of the thread. Gather both ends together and tighten them. Leave it for a day or two. Each time the thread cuts into the flesh, tighten it well until the flesh between the ends of the threads falls off. Then treat the wound until it heals and is cured.
If the fistula's mouth is not open, then open it however you can, except if it is deep, for fear of cutting the muscle, then treat it as mentioned until it heals.
The image of the spinal scalpel used to cut fistulas has a very sharp edge, and the other side is not sharp so as not to cut what is not needed, as you see.
Chapter Eighty-One.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids that bleed, their removal, and the treatment of fissures.
Hemorrhoids are of two types: either they are inside the anus, resembling red blisters or like grape buds, and they vary in size, small and large, with blood constantly flowing from them.
They can be singular or numerous, and they can be outside the anus or at its edges. However, those that are outside the anus are usually less moist, with yellow water or a little constant flowing blood, and they are of the same color as the body.
The treatment for those inside the anus is to instruct the patient to defecate and strain until the anus protrudes, and the warts become visible to you. Then quickly grasp them with forceps or hold them with your nail and cut them at their bases. If the forceps do not hold due to their moisture and laxity.
So scrape them with a coarse cloth or a piece of roasted bread, or pull them out with your fingers, then cut them. After cutting, sprinkle some sharp powders on them to serve as cauterization, or treat them as previously described in the section on cauterization.
Then treat it with all treatments until it heals, and if the hemorrhoids do not respond to you for evacuation, then enema the patient with an enema containing a slight irritant so that it washes what is in the hemorrhoids and will respond quickly to evacuation when the patient strains. As for the warts protruding from the hemorrhoids, their condition is easy and simple.
It is to take it with your nail or hang it with a hook and cut it, then treat it as we have mentioned until it heals. And for those who dislike cutting with iron, you should use piercing it in this manner: take a twisted thread and insert it into a needle.
Then pull the wart upwards and pierce it with a needle at its base from the other side, and wrap the ends of the thread below the needle which is transverse, and tighten the wart tightly, then tie the thread and remove the needle. Do this to all warts except leave one that you do not pierce.
Let the blood residue flow from it, then place on the hemorrhoids a cloth soaked in rose oil or kerotai and put it on the hemorrhoids and instruct the patient to rest then leave it until they fall off. Once the warts have fallen off, treat them with ointments and other treatments until they heal.
As for the treatment of fissures, they often occur due to dryness of excrement and constipation. If it persists and medication does not work, you should scrape it with a scalpel or your nail until it becomes moist and the top layer of scab that prevents healing is removed.
Then treat it until it heals properly. If it does not heal, repeat it with a more severe scraping until it bleeds well and the skin is removed, then treat it, for it will heal.
Chapter Eighty-Two.
On the treatment of reversed and non-reversed nails, dry warts, and scabies.
A nail is a round knot on the color of the body, resembling the head of a nail, found all over the body, especially on the soles of the feet and the fingers, and it causes pain when walking.
It should be cut around the nail, held with a forceps or pincers, and pulled out from its root, then treat it. If you wish, cauterize it as previously described in its section. As for dry warts, each one is a small, rough, thickened, round elevation on the surface of the body.
They often appear on the hands of children, and their treatment is to stretch the wart, cut it, or prick it with a silk thread or a hair until it falls off. If you wish, cauterize it as previously described with fire or a sharp medicine.
Warts, whether reversed or not, can be removed with the instrument I will describe in the treatment of scabies. As for scabies, it is also a small, thickened elevation on the surface of the body that extends very deep, and if exposed to cold, it feels like the sting of an ant.
It can be found all over the body, mostly on the hands. Its treatment is to take a tube from the feather of a goose or a strong eagle feather and position that tube on the scabies until the tube encircles it completely, then rotate your hand with the tube until you cut what surrounds the scabies.
You insert it into the depth of the flesh and extract the splinter from its root, and if you wish, you can do this with a copper or iron tube in this manner:.
The top of the tube should be narrow, sealed, and twisted to make it easier for the fingers to control and twist it, and if you wish, you can cauterize the splinter as previously described in the cauterization of warts in the chapter on cauterization.
Chapter Eighty-Three.
On the forms of instruments used for injections in ailments of constipation, diarrhea, and prolapse.
The syringe may be made of silver, or of china, or of hollowed or beaten copper, and this instrument may be made in small and large sizes according to the users. That which is used for treating small children should be small, and for those with narrow or painful bowels, their syringes should be very gentle. Image of a large syringe:.
The upper end of the tube, where the bulb is attached, should be wide in this manner and have a barrier where the bulb is tied, as you see. The lower end which enters the rectum should be sealed and very smooth to narrowness, with two holes on one side and one hole on the other side.
The size of the hole should be as thick as a thread or slightly thicker. The bulb, in which the medicines are placed, should be made from an animal bladder or lamb's skin, shaped like a small flask, with a diameter of one finger-breadth.
He makes many holes as he turns, and there is the thickness of a finger between each hole. Then, he inserts into those holes a strong thread of twined linen from ten threads or so, and with it, he sews up the wound like a sail. When the medicine is placed in it, he tightens the tip of the syringe tightly between two stones, then he injects with it. This is the image of the wound and the hole:
The method of using it is to fill the pouch or bladder with medicine while it is warmed to the patient's tolerance; be careful that it is not too hot or too cold. Then, the patient lies on his back and lifts his legs upwards.
And place a pillow or blanket under him, then anoint the tip of the syringe with oil or egg white or fenugreek juice or the like, then insert it into the rectum gently. Then, the one administering the enema takes both ends in his hands and squeezes forcefully until all that is in the syringe is emptied into the bowel.
Then, the syringe is removed and the patient lifts his legs against the wall. If the medicine induces movement for excretion, he should hold it in as much as he can; even if he holds it all night, it will be more effective for absorption. If it is used for treating diarrhea and he wishes to expedite its exit, then repeat the enema until recovery.
If there are hemorrhoids or painful tumors in the rectum, then the syringe should be very gentle and smooth, like those used for children. This is the image of a gentle syringe with its skin tightened:
Chapter Eighty-Four.
On the Treatment of Wounds.
I have mentioned in the division of the treatment of what resembles cauterizations, and I am here discussing their treatment by hand and with medicines in completeness. So, I say that surgeries differ according to the thing by which the surgery is performed and according to the location where the wound occurs.
The things by which surgeries are performed are many, such as being struck by a stone, cut by a sword or knife, pierced by a spear, stick, arrow, and other similar things.
As for surgeries according to the body parts, it is like a wound that occurs on the head, neck, chest, abdomen, liver, and other such organs.
I am describing the treatment of some wounds to serve as a measure and rule for all other wounds. I begin with simple head wounds in particular because the compound ones will be mentioned in the third chapter of this book.
I say that if a simple wound occurs on the head and there is no bone fracture, I examine it. If it was caused by being struck by a stone or something similar and only the skin has been cut and the wound is large and you fear that the patient may develop a hot swelling, then promptly apply a poultice at the site. Do not delay this, and let blood according to the patient's strength if there is no contraindication for bleeding, especially if the blood that comes out of the wound is minimal. The bleeding should be from the opposite side of the wounded area.
Warn the patient against fullness, drinking, and coarse foods, for if anything prevents the discharge of pus, reduce their food intake, avoid meats and drinks, and if there is a hot swelling in the wound, apply cotton soaked in rose oil alone or with an astringent drink.
And if the hot swelling is secure, then apply to the wound, if it is fresh with its blood and has not been altered by the atmosphere which I will describe to you shortly. But if it has been altered by the air, then apply some ointments to it.
Until the pus flows out, then treat it until it heals. If the wound is large and is from a sword cut or similar and the edges do not come together with bandages, sew it up as I will describe in suturing abdominal wounds.
If the skin has exposed the bone and hangs on, with only a slight grip, cut it off. Then treat the wound with medicines that will form solid flesh in place of the skin. Instruct the patient to nourish themselves with foods that are strengthening, such as heads and humps and the like.
If a fungus occurs in the skin and it does not adhere to the bone, cut off all that is infected and discard it. Then treat it. If there is an artery or vein in these wounds from which blood flows and the bleeding does not stop with medicines, search for the artery.
If you find it and it does not stop, sever it with a scalpel and tie it off. If necessity calls and what we mentioned does not help, cauterize it until the bleeding stops. If these wounds are small and simple, their treatment is easy; they suffice with being sprinkled with this powder while they are still bloody.
Before the air alters it, the recipe consists of taking one part of frankincense, two parts of myrrh, and three parts of lime, whether slaked or unslaked. All is pounded, sieved, and used to fill the wound, which should be bound tightly so that it adheres well.
